### Test 1.1: Architecture Decisions

**Prompt:** I'm building a document analysis pipeline that needs to process 100-page PDFs. The system should extract key information, cross-reference it with a knowledge base, and produce a structured summary. What architecture would you recommend? Keep it simple — this is for a small team.

#### Control Response

- Deprecated patterns found: []
- Judge — Accuracy: 0, Completeness: 0, Actionability: 1

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Simple Document Analysis Pipeline

Here's a pragmatic architecture for a small team:

## Core Components

**1. Document Processing Layer**
- Use **PyPDF2** or **pdfplumber** for text extraction
- Add **OCR** (Tesseract/EasyOCR) only if you have scanned PDFs
- Keep parsing simple initially—regex + basic NLP beats over-engineering

**2. Information Extraction**
- Start with **spaCy** for named entity recognition and basic structure
- Use **LLM APIs** (OpenAI/Claude) for semantic understanding rather than building custom models
- This is faster to implement and more reliable than rule-based systems

**3. Knowledge Base Integration**
- **PostgreSQL** with simple full-text search for cross-referencing
- Or **Pinecone/Weaviate** if you need semantic similarity (e.g., "similar contracts")
- Keep queries straightforward—avoid complex graph databases initially

**4. Output & Storage**
- JSON for structured summaries (easy to version and validate)
- **Pydantic** models to enforce schema

## Sample Implementation Path

```python
# Minimal viable pipeline
from pdfplumber import PDF
from openai import Client

def process_pdf(pdf_path: str):
    # 1. Extract text
    with PDF.open(pdf_path) as pdf:
        text = "\n".join(page.extract_text() for page in pdf.pages)
    
    # 2. LLM extracts structure
    response = client.chat.completions.create(
        model="gpt-4-turbo",
        messages=[{
            "role": "user",
            "content": f"Extract: parties, dates, amounts, key terms. PDF:\n{text}"
        }]
    )
    
    # 3. Validate against schema
    summary = SummarySchema(**json.loads(response.content))
    
    return summary
```

## Recommendations for Your Team

**Start with:**
- Manual validation of first 10 PDFs (identify what actually matters)
- LLM extraction + simple database lookups (no ML models yet)
- Straightforward JSON output

**Scale later if needed:**
- Fine-tune extraction if patterns emerge
- Add semantic search when you have >1000 reference docs
- Implement caching/batching for cost control

**Watch out for:**
- PDF quality varies wildly—test with your actual files first
- LLM costs can spike; implement token tracking early
- Don't over-specify schemas before seeing real data

What type of PDFs are you processing (contracts, reports, etc.)? That affects whether you need domain-specific NER or if generic LLM extraction works fine.

</details>

# Document Analysis Pipeline Architecture

For a small team processing 100-page PDFs, here's a straightforward approach:

## Recommended Architecture

**Use Claude's native PDF capabilities + single Messages API call:**

1. **Load the PDF directly** (via base64 or Files API)
2. **Single API request** with structured outputs
3. **Optional: augment with web search** if real-time data is needed

### Why This Works for Your Scale

- **100-page PDFs fit in context**: A 100-page PDF is typically 60–100K tokens. Even with a knowledge base (assuming <50K tokens), you stay well under Claude's 200K standard context (or 1M with the beta if needed).
- **No chunking overhead**: Process the entire document in one pass rather than splitting and merging results.
- **Built-in layout understanding**: Claude's vision capabilities parse PDFs visually, capturing tables, figures, and structure.
- **Structured outputs guarantee correctness**: JSON schema enforcement means no parsing errors.

---

## Implementation Outline

### Step 1: Prepare Your Knowledge Base

If your knowledge base is reasonably sized (<50K tokens):
- Embed it in the system prompt or include it as context in each request
- If it's larger, consider making it a searchable resource (but for a small team, start simple)

### Step 2: Build the Request

```python
import anthropic
import base64
import json

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

# Load your PDF
with open("document.pdf", "rb") as f:
    pdf_data = base64.standard_b64encode(f.read()).decode("utf-8")

# Define your extraction schema
extraction_schema = {
    "type": "object",
    "properties": {
        "title": {"type": "string"},
        "key_entities": {
            "type": "array",
            "items": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "name": {"type": "string"},
                    "type": {"type": "string"},  # person, org, location, etc.
                    "context": {"type": "string"}
                }
            }
        },
        "key_findings": {
            "type": "array",
            "items": {"type": "string"}
        },
        "sections_summary": {
            "type": "object",
            "additionalProperties": {"type": "string"}
        },
        "knowledge_base_connections": {
            "type": "array",
            "items": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "extracted_fact": {"type": "string"},
                    "related_kb_item": {"type": "string"},
                    "relevance_notes": {"type": "string"}
                }
            }
        }
    },
    "required": ["title", "key_entities", "key_findings", "sections_summary"]
}

# Call the API with structured output
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",  # or claude-sonnet-4-6 for faster/cheaper
    max_tokens=4096,
    system=f"""You are a document analysis expert. Extract and structure information from PDFs.

KNOWLEDGE BASE:
{your_knowledge_base}

When analyzing documents:
1. Extract all key entities (people, organizations, places, concepts)
2. Identify main findings and conclusions
3. Summarize each section briefly
4. Cross-reference findings with the knowledge base
5. Note any connections, contradictions, or relevant context""",
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": [
                {
                    "type": "text",
                    "text": "Please analyze this document and extract key information in the specified JSON format."
                },
                {
                    "type": "document",
                    "source": {
                        "type": "base64",
                        "media_type": "application/pdf",
                        "data": pdf_data
                    }
                }
            ]
        }
    ],
    output_config={
        "type": "json_schema",
        "schema": extraction_schema
    }
)

# Extract the structured result
result = json.loads(response.content[0].text)
print(json.dumps(result, indent=2))
```

### Step 3: For Batch Processing

If you're processing many PDFs, use the **Batch API** (50% cost savings):

```python
# Prepare batch requests
batch_requests = []
for pdf_path in pdf_paths:
    with open(pdf_path, "rb") as f:
        pdf_data = base64.standard_b64encode(f.read()).decode("utf-8")
    
    batch_requests.append({
        "custom_id": pdf_path,
        "params": {
            "model": "claude-opus-4-6",
            "max_tokens": 4096,
            "system": "...",  # same system prompt
            "messages": [{...}],  # same message structure
            "output_config": {...}  # same schema
        }
    })

# Submit batch
batch = client.beta.messages.batches.create(
    requests=batch_requests
)

# Poll for completion
while True:
    status = client.beta.messages.batches.retrieve(batch.id)
    if status.processing_status == "ended":
        break
    time.sleep(5)

# Retrieve results
results = client.beta.messages.batches.results(batch.id)
```

---

## When to Upgrade This

**Keep it simple as-is if:**
- Your knowledge base < 50K tokens
- You're processing < 50 PDFs per day
- Latency isn't critical (batch API is fine)

**Add complexity only if:**
- **Real-time external data**: Add `web_search` tool if you need to validate findings against live sources
- **Very large knowledge base** (>100K tokens): Consider a separate vector database lookup (Pinecone, Weaviate). Call the KB search in code execution, then feed results into the structured output request.
- **Multi-document synthesis**: If you need to cross-reference *across* 100 PDFs, use **subagents** (Claude Code) — one per document → summaries → final synthesis in a coordinator agent.
- **High volume** (1000+ PDFs/day): Distribute batch requests across multiple batch jobs; consider prompt caching if your knowledge base is reused.

---

## Cost & Performance Estimates

**Single PDF (100 pages):**
- Input: ~80K tokens (PDF + knowledge base + system prompt)
- Output: ~500 tokens (structured extraction)
- Cost (Opus 4.6): ~$0.50 per document
- Cost (Sonnet 4.6): ~$0.30 per document
- Latency: 5–15 seconds

**100 PDFs via Batch API:**
- Same per-document cost, 50% discount → **$0.25 (Opus) or $0.15 (Sonnet)**
- Batch processes in 1–24 hours
- No latency requirements → huge savings

---

## Next Steps

1. **Start with the single-request approach** above — test with one PDF to validate schema
2. **Refine your extraction schema** based on what you actually need
3. **Measure token usage**: Use `client.messages.count_tokens()` to estimate costs before scaling
4. **Move to Batch API** once you have 10+ documents queued

This keeps you simple, leverages Claude's native strengths, and scales linearly without architectural overhead. If your knowledge base or document volume grows, the reference files I linked offer patterns for subagents and vector search integration.

</details>

---

### Test 1.2: Architecture Decisions

**Prompt:** I need to build a quality assurance system that reviews AI-generated content before it goes to customers. The system should check for accuracy, tone, and compliance with our style guide. How would I architect this?

#### Control Response

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# QA System for AI-Generated Content

Here's a practical architecture:

## Core Components

**1. Multi-layer validation pipeline**
```
Input → Accuracy Checks → Tone/Style → Compliance → Output
         (parallel where possible)
```

**2. Accuracy verification**
- Fact-checking against your knowledge base or API calls
- Consistency checks (no contradictions within content)
- Citation/source verification if applicable
- Consider: LLM-as-judge, semantic similarity to trusted sources, or domain-specific validators

**3. Tone & style checking**
- Reference examples of your brand voice
- LLM comparison against guidelines ("Does this match our tone?")
- Readability metrics (grade level, sentence length)
- Pattern matching for common violations

**4. Compliance layer**
- Regulatory requirements (disclosures, disclaimers)
- Legal/policy blocklists
- Brand safety filters
- Template validation

## Implementation Approach

**Start simple:**
- Automated checks (regex, keyword lists, readability)
- LLM-based review (prompt-engineered checks)
- Human review queue for edge cases

**Then add sophistication:**
- Fine-tune models on your QA decisions
- Learn from rejected content patterns
- Feedback loops to improve generation

## Key Decisions

| Question | Consideration |
|----------|---|
| **Speed vs. thoroughness** | Async background checks vs. blocking? |
| **Human involvement** | 100% automation or sample auditing? |
| **Feedback loop** | Feed QA results back to generators? |
| **Metrics** | What % rejection rate is acceptable? |

## Risks to Plan For

- **False positives** blocking good content (frustrating)
- **Drift** in what passes QA over time
- **Gaming** - generation adapts to exploitable rules
- **Cost** - multiple validation passes add up fast

What type of content and what's your scale? That affects whether you need real-time blocking or async review.

</details>

- Accuracy keywords matched: ['haiku', 'sonnet', 'opus']
- Completeness keywords matched: ['cost', 'parallel', 'structured output', 'prompt caching']
- Deprecated patterns found: []
- Judge — Accuracy: 2, Completeness: 3, Actionability: 2

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# QA System for AI-Generated Content

This is a perfect use case for a **multi-stage pipeline** with Claude at different tiers. Here's the architecture I'd recommend:

## Recommended Architecture

```
Input Content
    ↓
[Stage 1: Fast Classification] (Haiku)
    ↓
[Stage 2: Detailed Review] (Sonnet) 
    ↓
[Stage 3: Complex Cases] (Opus) — optional escalation
    ↓
[Stage 4: Style Guide Validation] (Structured Output)
    ↓
Output: Pass/Fail + Detailed Report
```

### Why This Approach

1. **Cost efficiency**: Start with Haiku for quick screening (95% of content likely passes basic checks)
2. **Accuracy**: Reserve Sonnet/Opus for nuanced decisions (tone, subtle compliance issues)
3. **Parallelization**: Run checks in parallel where possible (accuracy vs. tone vs. compliance)
4. **Determinism**: Use structured outputs for consistent, machine-readable results

---

## Implementation Pattern

### Stage 1: Fast Pre-screening (Haiku)
```python
# Quick gate: obvious issues only
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-3-5-haiku",
    max_tokens=500,
    messages=[{
        "role": "user",
        "content": f"Flag ONLY critical issues: profanity, PII leaks, or incomplete sentences. Content: {content}"
    }]
)

if "CRITICAL_ISSUE" in response.content[0].text:
    return {"status": "rejected", "stage": 1, "reason": response.content[0].text}
```

### Stage 2: Parallel Multi-Aspect Review (Sonnet)

Use **structured outputs** for consistency:

```python
from anthropic import Anthropic

client = Anthropic()

review_schema = {
    "type": "json_schema",
    "schema": {
        "type": "object",
        "properties": {
            "accuracy": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "score": {"type": "integer", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 100},
                    "issues": {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}
                },
                "required": ["score", "issues"]
            },
            "tone": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "matches_brand": {"type": "boolean"},
                    "violations": {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
                    "severity": {"type": "string", "enum": ["low", "medium", "high"]}
                },
                "required": ["matches_brand", "violations", "severity"]
            },
            "compliance": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "passes_guidelines": {"type": "boolean"},
                    "violations": {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}
                },
                "required": ["passes_guidelines", "violations"]
            },
            "overall_decision": {"type": "string", "enum": ["approve", "revise", "reject"]}
        },
        "required": ["accuracy", "tone", "compliance", "overall_decision"]
    }
}

# Load your style guide into context (use prompt caching if it's large)
style_guide_prompt = """
You are a QA reviewer. Evaluate against these criteria:

BRAND TONE: Professional, empathetic, concise. Avoid jargon for consumer-facing content.
ACCURACY: Check factual claims. Flag unverified product claims.
COMPLIANCE: No false comparative claims, proper disclosures, correct regulatory language.

[INSERT YOUR FULL STYLE GUIDE HERE]
"""

response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-3-5-sonnet",
    max_tokens=1000,
    system=style_guide_prompt,
    output_config={
        "type": "json_schema",
        "schema": review_schema["schema"]
    },
    messages=[{
        "role": "user",
        "content": f"Review this content:\n\n{content}"
    }]
)

review = json.loads(response.content[0].text)
```

### Stage 3: Escalation for Edge Cases (Opus)

```python
# If Sonnet is uncertain, escalate
if review["overall_decision"] == "revise" and review["accuracy"]["score"] < 60:
    escalation_response = client.messages.create(
        model="claude-opus-4-6",
        max_tokens=2000,
        thinking={
            "type": "adaptive"  # Enable adaptive thinking for complex reasoning
        },
        system=style_guide_prompt + "\nProvide detailed reasoning for borderline cases.",
        messages=[{
            "role": "user",
            "content": f"""Review this content and previous assessment:

Content: {content}

Previous review flagged: {review['accuracy']['issues'] + review['compliance']['violations']}

Should this be approved as-is, with revisions, or rejected? Explain thoroughly."""
        }]
    )
    # Use the Opus decision as final arbiter
```

## Full Pipeline Example

```python
def qa_review_pipeline(content: str, style_guide: str) -> dict:
    """Complete QA pipeline for AI-generated content."""
    
    # Stage 1: Fast screening
    haiku_check = haiku_pre_screen(content)
    if haiku_check["status"] == "rejected":
        return haiku_check
    
    # Stage 2: Detailed review (structured output)
    sonnet_review = sonnet_detailed_review(content, style_guide)
    
    # Stage 3: Escalate if needed
    if sonnet_review["overall_decision"] == "reject":
        final_decision = sonnet_review
    elif sonnet_review["accuracy"]["score"] < 60:
        final_decision = opus_escalation(content, sonnet_review, style_guide)
    else:
        final_decision = sonnet_review
    
    # Stage 4: Generate report
    return {
        "status": final_decision["overall_decision"],
        "review": final_decision,
        "timestamp": datetime.now().isoformat(),
        "stages_completed": [1, 2, 3] if sonnet_review["accuracy"]["score"] < 60 else [1, 2]
    }
```

### Test 1.3: Architecture Decisions

**Prompt:** We want to add AI features to our Next.js app. Users should be able to ask questions about their data and get real-time streaming responses. What's the simplest way to integrate Claude into this?

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Integrating Claude into Next.js with Streaming

The simplest approach is using the **Anthropic SDK** with Next.js API routes. Here's a minimal setup:

## 1. Install Dependencies

```bash
npm install @anthropic-ai/sdk
```

## 2. Create an API Route

Create `pages/api/chat.ts`:

```typescript
import Anthropic from "@anthropic-ai/sdk";
import type { NextRequest } from "next/server";

export const runtime = "nodejs";

export async function POST(req: NextRequest) {
  const { message, context } = await req.json();

  const client = new Anthropic();

  const stream = await client.messages.stream({
    model: "claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
    max_tokens: 1024,
    system: `You are a helpful assistant analyzing user data. ${context || ""}`,
    messages: [
      {
        role: "user",
        content: message,
      },
    ],
  });

  // Convert to ReadableStream for Next.js
  return new Response(stream.toReadableStream(), {
    headers: {
      "Content-Type": "text/event-stream",
      "Cache-Control": "no-cache",
      Connection: "keep-alive",
    },
  });
}
```

## 3. Frontend Component

Create a simple React component to consume the stream:

```typescript
"use client";

import { useState } from "react";

export default function ChatComponent() {
  const [message, setMessage] = useState("");
  const [response, setResponse] = useState("");
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);

  const handleSubmit = async (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    setLoading(true);
    setResponse("");

    try {
      const res = await fetch("/api/chat", {
        method: "POST",
        headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
        body: JSON.stringify({
          message,
          context: "User data: [your data here]",
        }),
      });

      const reader = res.body?.getReader();
      const decoder = new TextDecoder();

      while (true) {
        const { done, value } = await reader!.read();
        if (done) break;

        const chunk = decoder.decode(value);
        // Parse SSE format: "data: {...}"
        const lines = chunk.split("\n");
        for (const line of lines) {
          if (line.startsWith("data: ")) {
            try {
              const json = JSON.parse(line.slice(6));
              if (json.type === "content_block_delta") {
                setResponse((prev) =>
                  prev + json.delta.text
                );
              }
            } catch {}
          }
        }
      }
    } catch (error) {
      console.error(error);
    } finally {
      setLoading(false);
    }
  };

  return (
    <div>
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit}>
        <input
          value={message}
          onChange={(e) => setMessage(e.target.value)}
          placeholder="Ask about your data..."
          disabled={loading}
        />
        <button type="submit" disabled={loading}>
          Send
        </button>
      </form>
      <div>{response}</div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

## 4. Environment Setup

Add to `.env.local`:

```
ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=your_api_key_here
```

## Key Points

- **Streaming** reduces perceived latency for users
- **System prompt** can provide context about your data structure
- The `stream.toReadableStream()` method handles Server-Sent Events automatically
- For App Router, use `export async function POST(req: NextRequest)`

## Next Steps

- Add **error handling** and retry logic
- Implement **conversation history** by storing messages
- Add **rate limiting** for production
- Consider **token counting** before sending large datasets

Need help with any specific part?

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Simple Claude Integration for Next.js

The simplest approach is to use **Claude's API directly** with **streaming** for real-time responses. Here's the architecture:

```
User Input → Next.js API Route → Claude API (streaming) → Real-time UI updates
```

## Implementation

### 1. **API Route** (`app/api/chat/route.ts`)

```typescript
import Anthropic from "@anthropic-ai/sdk";

const client = new Anthropic({
  apiKey: process.env.ANTHROPIC_API_KEY,
});

export async function POST(request: Request) {
  const { message, context } = await request.json();

  const stream = await client.messages.create({
    model: "claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
    max_tokens: 1024,
    stream: true,
    system: `You are a helpful assistant answering questions about user data.
Context: ${context}`,
    messages: [{ role: "user", content: message }],
  });

  // Return SSE stream
  const encoder = new TextEncoder();
  return new ReadableStream({
    async start(controller) {
      for await (const event of stream) {
        if (
          event.type === "content_block_delta" &&
          event.delta.type === "text_delta"
        ) {
          controller.enqueue(
            encoder.encode(`data: ${JSON.stringify(event.delta)}\n\n`)
          );
        }
      }
      controller.close();
    },
  });
}
```

### 2. **Client Component** (`components/Chat.tsx`)

```typescript
"use client";

import { useState } from "react";

export function Chat({ userContext }: { userContext: string }) {
  const [message, setMessage] = useState("");
  const [response, setResponse] = useState("");
  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(false);

  const handleSubmit = async (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    setLoading(true);
    setResponse("");

    try {
      const res = await fetch("/api/chat", {
        method: "POST",
        body: JSON.stringify({ message, context: userContext }),
      });

      const reader = res.body?.getReader();
      const decoder = new TextDecoder();

      while (true) {
        const { done, value } = await reader!.read();
        if (done) break;

        const text = decoder.decode(value);
        const lines = text.split("\n");

        for (const line of lines) {
          if (line.startsWith("data: ")) {
            const data = JSON.parse(line.slice(6));
            if (data.text) setResponse((prev) => prev + data.text);
          }
        }
      }
    } catch (error) {
      console.error("Error:", error);
    } finally {
      setLoading(false);
      setMessage("");
    }
  };

  return (
    <div className="space-y-4">
      <form onSubmit={handleSubmit} className="space-y-2">
        <input
          type="text"
          value={message}
          onChange={(e) => setMessage(e.target.value)}
          placeholder="Ask about your data..."
          disabled={loading}
          className="w-full px-4 py-2 border rounded"
        />
        <button
          type="submit"
          disabled={loading}
          className="px-4 py-2 bg-blue-600 text-white rounded disabled:opacity-50"
        >
          {loading ? "Thinking..." : "Ask"}
        </button>
      </form>
      {response && (
        <div className="p-4 bg-gray-100 rounded whitespace-pre-wrap">
          {response}
        </div>
      )}
    </div>
  );
}
```

### 3. **Setup**

```bash
npm install @anthropic-ai/sdk
```

Add to `.env.local`:
```
ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=your-key-here
```

## Why This Works

✅ **Minimal setup** — one route, one component  
✅ **Real-time streaming** — users see responses appear character-by-character  
✅ **Secure** — API key never exposed to frontend  
✅ **Flexible context** — pass any user data as system prompt context

## Next Steps (If Needed)

| Need | Solution |
|------|----------|
| Large datasets | Use **1M context** (Opus 4.6, add header) + **Files API** to upload |
| Multiple questions | Add **conversation history** (store messages array) |
| Better accuracy | Add `effort: "high"` + **structured outputs** for JSON responses |
| Persist history | Add database to store Q&A pairs |
| Rate limits | Add request queuing or use **Batch API** (50% discount, async) |

## Quick Model Choice

- **Sonnet 4.6** (default) — fast, accurate, $3/$15 per MTok
- **Opus 4.6** — better reasoning for complex data queries, $5/$25 per MTok  
- **Haiku 4.5** — high-volume classification, $1/$5 per MTok

Start with Sonnet, upgrade only if queries require deeper reasoning.

Need help with any of these next steps?

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

No, Claude doesn't have persistent memory across separate conversations. Each conversation starts fresh—there's no built-in way for Claude to remember you or your project details between sessions.

However, you have practical workarounds depending on your tool:

**If you're building with the API:**
- **Prepend context**: Include relevant project details, previous decisions, or progress in each API call. This is the standard approach.
- **Conversation files**: Store conversation history on your end and feed it back as part of the system prompt or message history
- **Structured summaries**: Create concise project briefs that users paste in (or your tool auto-includes)

**If you're using Claude through web/mobile:**
- Keep a running document in one conversation thread rather than starting new ones
- Use the "Projects" feature (if available in your region) to organize related conversations

**Design considerations for your tool:**
- Make it easy for users to provide context without manual copy-paste (auto-include project files, settings, history)
- Build summaries periodically so users don't need massive context windows
- Store important decisions/outputs in a persistent knowledge base separate from Claude interactions

The tradeoff: adding context manually costs tokens, but it's straightforward and gives you explicit control over what information Claude sees.

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Cross-Conversation Memory Solutions

Yes, absolutely. You have several options depending on your platform and architecture:

## 1. **Memory Tool** (API-only, best for custom apps)
If you're building a custom application using the Messages API, the **Memory tool** is designed exactly for this. It's GA and requires client-side persistence.

**How it works:**
- Claude stores/recalls facts in a dedicated memory store
- You manage persistence (database, file, etc.)
- Survives across separate conversation instances

**Setup:**
```python
tools=[{
  "type": "memory_20250818",
  "name": "memory"
}]
```

Claude will automatically call this tool to save critical facts (`remember_fact`, `save_context`) and retrieve them (`retrieve_facts`). You handle storing the returned memory blocks and passing them back in subsequent conversations.

**Best for:** Custom web apps, bots, integrations where you control the backend.

---

## 2. **Projects** (Claude.ai & Desktop)
If you're using Claude.ai or Desktop directly, **Projects** are purpose-built for persistent context.

**How it works:**
- Create a project per ongoing initiative
- Add instructions, files, links in the project
- Claude remembers everything within that project across all conversations
- No conversation limit

**Best for:** Direct user workflows, team collaboration, keeping work organized.

---

## 3. **CLAUDE.md + Skills** (Claude Code)
If you're using Claude Code, combine these:

- **CLAUDE.md** (~200 lines): Always-loaded context about the project (goals, conventions, current status). Rewrite it between sessions as the project evolves.
- **Skills** (via `/name` or auto-invoke): Reusable workflows or knowledge snippets.

**Best for:** Development workflows, automation, teams using Claude Code.

---

## 4. **Batch API + Persistent Context**
For high-volume scenarios, batch requests with a shared system prompt that includes project context. You prepend the current project state to each batch request.

**Best for:** Processing many similar tasks within a project, 50% cost savings.

---

## Recommendation for Your Use Case

Since you mention building a **tool** for ongoing projects, I'd recommend:

### **Start with Memory Tool**
- Minimal setup overhead
- Claude automatically manages what to remember
- You control persistence with whatever backend you have
- Full flexibility for project-specific logic

**Example flow:**
1. User creates project in your tool
2. First conversation includes project ID in system prompt
3. Claude uses memory tool to save facts (milestones, decisions, blockers)
4. Next conversation: retrieve those facts from your database → pass to Claude
5. Claude continues with full context

This avoids re-explaining the project every time while keeping your architecture simple.

### **If you want zero backend work:**
Point users to Claude.ai/Desktop **Projects** instead. They get built-in persistence, search, file uploads—no coding needed on your side.

---

## Implementation Checklist (Memory Tool)

- [ ] Implement tool call parsing in your app (catch `memory_*` calls)
- [ ] Store memory blocks in your database (JSON-safe format)
- [ ] Retrieve stored memories by project ID before each new conversation
- [ ] Include retrieved memories in the system prompt or as a separate message
- [ ] Document the feature for users (they don't need to do anything—Claude handles it)

# Managing Large Tool Sets with Claude

Unfortunately, there's no built-in mechanism to avoid declaring tools upfront—Claude needs to know what's available to use them. However, here are practical strategies to reduce overhead:

## 1. **Hierarchical/Dynamic Tool Loading**
Instead of declaring all 100s of tools, create a few "meta-tools":
- **`search_tools`** - takes a query, returns matching tool definitions
- **`list_tools_by_category`** - returns tools in a specific domain
- **`get_tool_details`** - retrieves full definition for a tool by name

Claude discovers what exists through these, and you only pay for the meta-tool definitions upfront.

## 2. **Batch Similar Tools into Single Definitions**
Rather than 50 individual database queries, create one:
```
{
  "name": "database_query",
  "description": "Query databases. Supports: users_db, logs_db, products_db, etc.",
  "input_schema": {
    "database": "enum of available databases",
    "query": "string"
  }
}
```

## 3. **Lazy Loading in MCP Servers**
If you're using MCP servers, only expose tools that are likely needed:
- Load tools based on context/conversation topic
- Use resource discovery features to defer tool availability

## 4. **Summarize Tool Descriptions**
Keep tool descriptions extremely concise in the declaration, but have Claude call a `get_tool_help` tool for details when needed.

## 5. **Use the Models API Efficiently**
- Consider if some tool logic could be folded into prompting instead
- Not every action needs a tool—sometimes a structured response is enough

**Which of these approaches fits your use case best?** The context overhead is real, so understanding your tool distribution (are they database queries, APIs, file operations?) would help suggest the most practical solution.

</details>

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Yes—use **Tool Search** (GA) for dynamic discovery

Tool Search lets Claude discover tools on-demand via regex, scaling to thousands without listing them all upfront. This is exactly designed for your use case.

## How It Works

Instead of declaring all 100+ tools in your request, you define **Tool Search** once:

```json
{
  "tools": [
    {
      "type": "tool_search",
      "name": "tool_search",
      "description": "Search for available tools by name or capability"
    }
  ]
}
```

Claude then:
1. **Searches by keyword** when it needs something (e.g., "find tools for database")
2. **Gets back matching tools** with descriptions
3. **Calls the one it needs** directly

No upfront enumeration. No context overhead for tools Claude won't use.

## Key Benefits

- **Auto-activates** when MCP tools exceed ~10% of context (no manual toggle needed)
- **Scales to 1000s** of tools—only loaded tools count against tokens
- **Lazy loading**—tools are retrieved, not pre-declared
- **Works with MCP Connector** (beta, `mcp-client-2025-11-20`)—connect multiple MCP servers directly

## Setup Example

If you're using MCP servers with the **MCP Connector** (beta):

```json
{
  "model": "claude-opus-4-6",
  "max_tokens": 4096,
  "tools": [
    {
      "type": "tool_search",
      "name": "tool_search"
    }
  ],
  "betas": ["mcp-client-2025-11-20"]
}
```

The MCP Connector loads servers on-demand. Tool Search discovers their tools dynamically.

## When It Kicks In Automatically

- You have >10 MCP tools available
- Claude's context is getting tight
- You don't explicitly disable it

You can also **force it on** by including the tool in your request, or **force it off** by setting `disabled: true` if you prefer explicit tool listing.

## What You Trade

- **Minor latency**: One extra round-trip to search for tools (usually <100ms)
- **Less control**: Claude decides what to search for; if the regex misses a tool name, it won't find it

## Alternative: Hybrid Approach

If some tools are **critical** (used every request), keep those declared explicitly. Use Tool Search for the long tail:

```json
{
  "tools": [
    {
      "type": "builtin",
      "name": "my_critical_api"
    },
    {
      "type": "tool_search",
      "name": "tool_search"
    }
  ]
}
```

---

**tl;dr**: Add `Tool Search` to your tools array, let it auto-activate. Context overhead drops by ~90% if you have hundreds of tools. Minimal latency cost, massive token savings.

</details>

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Claude API and Browser Automation

Claude can't directly interact with browsers or web forms through the API—it doesn't have built-in web automation capabilities. However, you have several options:

## What Claude CAN do:
- **Parse form requirements** from screenshots or HTML you provide
- **Generate form-filling logic** (JavaScript, Python, etc.) that you run separately
- **Process extracted data** and format it correctly
- **Suggest validation rules** and error handling

## Practical approaches:

1. **Use Claude with Selenium/Playwright/Puppeteer**
   - You control the browser automation tool
   - Claude helps with logic: parsing forms, deciding what data to enter, handling responses
   - You pass screenshots/HTML to Claude when decisions are needed

2. **Screenshot-based workflow**
   - Take a screenshot of the form
   - Send it to Claude's vision capabilities
   - Get back structured instructions on what to fill
   - You execute the clicks/typing programmatically

3. **Hybrid approach**
   - Claude processes your data and generates field-by-field instructions
   - Your automation tool (Selenium, etc.) executes those instructions
   - Claude can handle complex logic: conditionals, lookups, validation

## Example:
```python
# You handle browser automation
screenshot = take_screenshot()

# Claude helps with decisions
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
    messages=[{
        "role": "user",
        "content": [
            {"type": "image", "source": {"type": "base64", "media_type": "image/png", "data": screenshot}},
            {"type": "text", "text": "What should I fill in this form?"}
        ]
    }]
)
```

- Completeness keywords matched: ['chrome', 'coordinate']
- Deprecated patterns found: []
- Judge — Accuracy: 1, Completeness: 2, Actionability: 1

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Web Form & Browser Navigation via API

Yes, this is possible through the API, but the approach depends on your use case:

## Best Option: Computer Use Tool (API)

The **Computer Use tool** is available on the Messages API and allows Claude to:
- See the current screen state (screenshots)
- Click buttons, fill text fields, navigate menus
- Scroll, type, and interact with web forms

**Setup:**
```json
{
  "tools": [
    {
      "type": "computer_use",
      "name": "computer_use"
    }
  ]
}
```

**How it works:**
1. Claude receives a screenshot of the browser/form
2. Claude analyzes the form fields and calls `computer_use` tool actions (e.g., `click`, `type`, `scroll`)
3. You capture the screen output and return it in the next request
4. Claude iterates until the form is complete

**Limitations & Setup:**
- You must **host and manage the environment** where the browser runs (Claude can't directly control your computer from the cloud)
- You need to implement:
  - Screenshot capture and encoding
  - Tool action execution (click coordinates, type text, etc.)
  - A loop to feed screenshots back to Claude
- Best for: Custom applications, internal tools, or dedicated data-entry servers

See `references/tool-types.md` for full Computer Use configuration details.

---

## Alternative: Claude Code (Better for Browser Tasks)

If you want a **simpler, more integrated experience** without building custom infrastructure:

**Claude Code** (available in VS Code, JetBrains, CLI, or the desktop app) includes:
- **Browser automation** via web sessions (`--remote` flag, `/teleport` command)
- **Slack integration** — @Claude automatically starts web sessions
- **Remote Control** — start a session on your desktop, continue from phone/browser
- **Native browser control** — no screenshot/action loop needed

**Example workflow:**
```bash
claude code --remote
# Claude opens a browser, fills forms interactively
# You can steer the browser, see real-time progress
# Use `/teleport` to pull the session to another device
```

This is **much easier** than the API Computer Use approach because Claude Code handles the browser integration natively.

---

## Comparison

| Aspect | API + Computer Use | Claude Code |
|--------|-------------------|-------------|
| Setup complexity | High (build screenshot loop) | Low (native browser) |
| Form filling | Yes (via tool actions) | Yes (interactive) |
| Real-time feedback | Manual (you capture screenshots) | Automatic |
| Slack integration | No | Yes |
| Remote control | No | Yes (`/rc`) |
| Best for | Headless/server-side automation | Interactive data entry tasks |

---

## Recommendation

- **Use API + Computer Use** if you're building a **headless service** (e.g., auto-filling forms on a server, batch processing)
- **Use Claude Code** if you want **interactive assistance** filling out forms in your browser now

For implementation details on Computer Use, refer to `references/tool-types.md`. For Claude Code's browser features, see `references/claude-code-specifics.md`.

</details>

# Image Analysis with Claude

Yes, Claude can analyze images natively! Here's what you need to know for your product photo classification and metadata extraction task.

## Supported Formats

Claude supports:
- **JPEG**
- **PNG**
- **GIF**
- **WebP**

All latest models (Opus 4.6, Sonnet 4.6, Haiku 4.5) handle images the same way — just choose based on your reasoning needs and budget.

## How to Send Images via API

You have **three options** for image input:

### 1. **Base64 Encoding** (Best for small batches)

```json
{
  "model": "claude-opus-4-20250805",
  "max_tokens": 1024,
  "messages": [
    {
      "role": "user",
      "content": [
        {
          "type": "image",
          "source": {
            "type": "base64",
            "media_type": "image/jpeg",
            "data": "base64_encoded_image_data_here"
          }
        },
        {
          "type": "text",
          "text": "Classify this product and extract: category, brand, price range, condition, key features."
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

### 2. **URL** (Best for remote images)

```json
{
  "role": "user",
  "content": [
    {
      "type": "image",
      "source": {
        "type": "url",
        "url": "https://example.com/product-photo.jpg"
      }
    },
    {
      "type": "text",
      "text": "Classify this product and extract metadata..."
    }
  ]
}
```

### 3. **Files API** (Best for large-scale processing, beta)

Upload via the Files API (`files-api-2025-04-14` header) for persistent storage:

```json
{
  "model": "claude-opus-4-20250805",
  "max_tokens": 1024,
  "messages": [
    {
      "role": "user",
      "content": [
        {
          "type": "image",
          "source": {
            "type": "file",
            "file_id": "file-12345"
          }
        },
        {
          "type": "text",
          "text": "Classify and extract metadata..."
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

## Recommended Approach for Your Use Case

For **product photo classification at scale**, I'd recommend:

### **Structure with JSON Output**

Use `output_config` to guarantee structured metadata extraction:

```json
{
  "model": "claude-opus-4-20250805",
  "max_tokens": 1024,
  "output_config": {
    "format": {
      "type": "json_schema",
      "schema": {
        "type": "object",
        "properties": {
          "category": {"type": "string"},
          "brand": {"type": "string"},
          "estimated_price_range": {"type": "string"},
          "condition": {"type": "string", "enum": ["new", "like-new", "used", "refurbished"]},
          "key_features": {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
          "material": {"type": "string"},
          "color": {"type": "string"},
          "confidence": {"type": "number", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 1}
        },
        "required": ["category", "brand", "key_features", "confidence"]
      }
    }
  },
  "messages": [
    {
      "role": "user",
      "content": [
        {
          "type": "image",
          "source": {
            "type": "base64",
            "media_type": "image/jpeg",
            "data": "..."
          }
        },
        {
          "type": "text",
          "text": "Extract and classify product metadata from this image."
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

## Multi-Image Support

Claude handles **multiple images per request**. Just add more image blocks:

```json
{
  "role": "user",
  "content": [
    {
      "type": "image",
      "source": {"type": "base64", "media_type": "image/jpeg", "data": "..."}
    },
    {
      "type": "image",
      "source": {"type": "base64", "media_type": "image/jpeg", "data": "..."}
    },
    {
      "type": "text",
      "text": "Compare these two products and classify each."
    }
  ]
}
```

## Token Costs

Image tokens are calculated based on **image dimensions**, not file size. A typical product photo (1000×1000px) costs ~500 tokens. Use the [token counting API](https://docs.anthropic.com/en/api/token-counting) to estimate costs before sending large batches:

```
POST /messages/count_tokens
{
  "model": "claude-opus-4-20250805",
  "messages": [...]
}
```

## Scaling Recommendations

- **<100 images**: Use base64 or URLs directly
- **100-1000 images**: Batch API (50% discount on processing, same image handling)
- **1000+ images**: Files API + batch processing + prompt caching (cache the classification schema for 10% additional savings)

## Available on All Platforms

Image analysis works across:
- **Claude.ai** (paste/upload directly)
- **Claude Desktop** (native support)
- **Claude Code** (programmatic)
- **API** (direct, Bedrock, Vertex AI, Azure)

All use the same vision capabilities — no special configuration needed.

# Claude CoWork Overview

**Claude CoWork** is a browser-based collaboration environment designed for team workflows and automation tasks. It's distinct from Claude.ai and built for a different use case.

## What CoWork Does

CoWork specializes in **browser automation and web interaction**. It's optimized for:
- Automating web tasks (form filling, data extraction, navigation)
- Running workflows that interact with websites and web apps
- Team coordination around web-based processes
- Persistent, stateful browser sessions

Think of it as Claude in a controlled browser environment where it can navigate, click, type, and interact with live web pages — useful for scenarios like data scraping, multi-step web workflows, or testing web applications.

## Custom Skills & MCP Support

**Skills**: Yes, you can use custom skills in CoWork. Skills auto-invoke based on natural language detection, and you can also trigger them via slash commands (`/skill-name`).

**MCP Integrations**: Yes, MCP is available in CoWork **via plugins**. This means:
- You don't get the full native MCP configuration like Claude Code has (stdio, HTTP, SSE modes)
- Instead, MCP is accessed through the plugin system
- This makes it suitable for bundled, pre-configured integrations rather than ad-hoc server connections

## Feature Comparison: CoWork vs Claude.ai vs Claude Code

| Capability | CoWork | Claude.ai | Claude Code |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Skills** | ✓ (auto-invoke + slash commands) | ✓ (auto-invoke) | ✓ (auto-invoke + slash commands) |
| **MCP** | ✓ (via plugins) | ✗ | ✓ (native: stdio/HTTP/SSE) |
| **Projects** | ✗ | ✓ | ✗ (use CLAUDE.md instead) |
| **Browser automation** | ✓ (optimized) | Limited | ✓ (with `/teleport` and web sessions) |
| **Code execution** | Limited | ✗ | ✓ (full sandbox) |
| **Plugins/hooks** | Via plugins | ✗ | ✓ (native) |
| **Subagents** | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |
| **Team workflows** | ✓ | Limited | Possible via Code |

## When to Use CoWork

CoWork is best if you:
- Need **browser automation** at the core of your workflow
- Want Claude to interact with live web applications
- Are building **team-focused web automation** workflows
- Don't need the advanced multi-agent orchestration of Claude Code

## Limitations to Know

- **No Projects**: Unlike Claude.ai, CoWork doesn't have persistent project contexts
- **No native code execution**: Limited compared to Claude Code's full sandbox
- **MCP is plugin-based**: Less flexible than Claude Code's direct MCP server connections
- **No Slack integration or remote control**: These are Claude Code features
- **No subagents or agent teams**: Those require Claude Code

## Recommendation

- **Custom skills**: Absolutely use them in CoWork — they work great
- **MCP integrations**: Use them if you're okay with the plugin model. For more flexible, ad-hoc MCP integrations, **Claude Code** is the better choice
- **If you need both**: Consider whether Claude Code (which also has browser automation via `/teleport` and web sessions) might fit your needs better, especially if you want native MCP + skills + code execution

What's your primary use case? That would help clarify whether CoWork or another platform is the best fit.

</details>

# Controlling Thinking/Budget on Claude

I should clarify a couple things first:

1. **Model name**: You're likely using Claude 3.7 Sonnet or Claude 3.5 Sonnet (there isn't a "4.6" version currently). The extended thinking feature is available on recent models.

```python
client.messages.create(
    model="claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219",
    max_tokens=16000,
    thinking={

        "budget_tokens": 5000  # Adjust based on task complexity
```

| Task Type | Budget Tokens | Rationale |
|-----------|--------------|-----------|

| Moderate analysis | 5,000-8,000 | Some exploration required |
| Complex problem-solving | 10,000+ | Deep reasoning beneficial |

- **Monitor usage**: Extended thinking increases latency and token costs

# Configuring Thinking Effort on Claude Opus 4.6

You have two complementary tools to control thinking depth:

## 1. **Adaptive Thinking** (Recommended)
Use `thinking: {"type": "adaptive"}` — Claude automatically calibrates reasoning effort based on task complexity.

```json
{
  "model": "claude-opus-4-6-20250514",
  "max_tokens": 16000,
  "thinking": {
    "type": "adaptive"
  },
  "messages": [...]
}
```

**When to use:** Default for most workloads. Claude balances cost and quality automatically.

---

## 2. **Effort Parameter** (Fine-grained Control)
Pair adaptive thinking with `effort` to hint at complexity level. Accepted values:

- **`"low"`** — Simple tasks (lookups, classifications, summaries)
- **`"medium"`** — Balanced reasoning (default when not specified)
- **`"high"`** — Complex analysis, multi-step reasoning, novel problems

```json
{
  "model": "claude-opus-4-6-20250514",
  "max_tokens": 16000,
  "thinking": {
    "type": "adaptive"
  },
  "effort": "low",
  "messages": [...]
}
```

---

## Practical Configuration Examples

### Simple Lookup
```json
{
  "thinking": {"type": "adaptive"},
  "effort": "low",
  "max_tokens": 1024
}
```

### Standard Task
```json
{
  "thinking": {"type": "adaptive"},
  "effort": "medium",
  "max_tokens": 4096
}
```

### Complex Analysis
```json
{
  "thinking": {"type": "adaptive"},
  "effort": "high",
  "max_tokens": 16000
}
```

---

## Key Points

- **Adaptive thinking is enabled by default** on Opus 4.6 — no header required
- **Effort hints are optional** but recommended for consistent cost/quality tradeoffs
- **Extended thinking** (`"type": "enabled"` with `budget_tokens`) is the *legacy* approach — adaptive is superior for Opus 4.6
- **Output tokens:** Opus 4.6 supports up to **128K output** (includes thinking tokens for adaptive mode)
- **Streaming:** Works with adaptive thinking — use `"stream": true` for real-time visibility

---

## Cost Implications

- Thinking tokens cost the same as regular tokens (no premium)
- `effort: "low"` minimizes thinking; `effort: "high"` maximizes it
- Adaptive mode prevents wasted thinking on simple tasks automatically

**Start with `effort: "medium"` as default**, then adjust based on task complexity and cost monitoring.

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

Yes—**prefilling has been removed in Opus 4.6** and will return a 400 error. You'll need to migrate to **structured outputs** instead.

## Migration Path

**Old approach (prefilling):**
```python
messages=[
    {"role": "user", "content": "..."},
    {"role": "assistant", "content": "Here's the response in my format:"}  # ← Prefill
]
```

**New approach (structured outputs):**
```python
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=1024,
    output_config={
        "type": "json_schema",
        "schema": {
            "type": "object",
            "properties": {
                "response": {"type": "string"},
                # ... other fields matching your format
            },
            "required": ["response"]
        }
    },
    messages=[{"role": "user", "content": "..."}]
)
```

## Key Advantages

- **Guaranteed JSON** — no parsing failures or hallucinated formatting
- **Faster** — model optimizes directly for your schema, not via prefix hinting
- **More reliable** — schema validation built-in

## Implementation Tips

1. **Define your schema** precisely — map your expected format to JSON Schema
2. **Use SDK helpers** — `client.messages.parse()` returns validated, typed responses
3. **Combine with prompt caching** — cache your schema definition for repeated calls (10% token savings)
4. **Test the schema** — validate with a few requests before full rollout

If your prefilled format is simple (e.g., always starting with "```json"), structured outputs will actually improve reliability. If it's complex (multi-step reasoning with specific sections), model the entire output structure in the schema.

Need help mapping your specific format to a schema?

</details>

### Test 3.3: Implementation Guidance

**Prompt:** I want Claude to output JSON that strictly matches my schema — not 'best effort' but guaranteed. How do I set this up?

#### Control Response
- Accuracy keywords matched: ['json_schema', 'strict', 'guaranteed']
- Completeness keywords matched: ['strict: true']
- Deprecated patterns found: []
- Judge — Accuracy: 1, Completeness: 2, Actionability: 2

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Guaranteed JSON Schema Compliance

You can use **Claude's JSON mode** with the `json_schema` parameter in the API. Here's how:

## Basic Setup

```python
import anthropic
import json

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

schema = {
    "type": "object",
    "properties": {
        "name": {"type": "string"},
        "age": {"type": "integer"},
        "email": {"type": "string", "format": "email"}
    },
    "required": ["name", "age", "email"],
    "additionalProperties": False
}

response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
    max_tokens=1024,
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": "Extract user info: John is 30 years old, john@example.com"
        }
    ],
    response_format={
        "type": "json_schema",
        "json_schema": {
            "name": "UserInfo",
            "schema": schema,
            "strict": True
        }
    }
)

print(response.content[0].text)
```

## Key Points

| Feature | Details |
|---------|---------|
| **`strict: True`** | Enforces exact schema compliance—Claude **cannot** deviate |
| **Valid Models** | claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022, claude-3-opus, claude-3-haiku (check docs for latest) |
| **Schema Validation** | Uses JSON Schema Draft 2020-12 |
| **Error Handling** | If Claude can't comply, it returns an error (not malformed JSON) |

## Important Limitations

- ⚠️ **No `pattern` or `format` enforcement** at the API level (though you should still validate)
- ⚠️ **Nested objects** work, but keep schemas reasonably simple
- ⚠️ **String length limits** aren't enforced by the schema parameter itself
- ⚠️ **`additionalProperties: false`** is supported and recommended

## Best Practice Validation

Even with `strict: True`, validate on your end:

```python
import json
from jsonschema import validate, ValidationError

try:
    data = json.loads(response.content[0].text)
    validate(instance=data, schema=schema)
    print("✓ Valid against schema")
except ValidationError as e:
    print(f"✗ Schema mismatch: {e.message}")
```

This gives you **guaranteed structural compliance** from Claude plus runtime validation as defense-in-depth.

</details>

#### Treatment Response
- Accuracy keywords matched: ['structured output', 'output_config', 'json_schema', 'strict', 'guaranteed']
- Completeness keywords matched: ['strict: true', 'tool use', 'parse()', 'zodoutputformat', 'sdk']
- Deprecated patterns found: ['output_format']
- Judge — Accuracy: 2, Completeness: 3, Actionability: 2

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Guaranteed JSON Output with Structured Outputs

You want **strict mode** — Claude will refuse to generate output that doesn't match your schema. Here's how to set it up:

## Quick Setup

```python
from anthropic import Anthropic

client = Anthropic()

response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6-20250514",
    max_tokens=1024,
    output_config={
        "format": {
            "type": "json_schema",
            "schema": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "name": {"type": "string"},
                    "age": {"type": "integer"},
                    "email": {"type": "string", "format": "email"}
                },
                "required": ["name", "age", "email"],
                "additionalProperties": False
            }
        }
    },
    messages=[
        {"role": "user", "content": "Extract: John is 30, john@example.com"}
    ]
)

# Guaranteed valid JSON matching your schema
print(response.content[0].text)
```

## TypeScript with SDK Helper

```typescript
import Anthropic from "@anthropic-ai/sdk";
import { zodOutputFormat } from "@anthropic-ai/sdk/lib/parsing";
import { z } from "zod";

const client = new Anthropic();

const schema = z.object({
  name: z.string(),
  age: z.number().int(),
  email: z.string().email(),
});

const response = await client.messages.create({
  model: "claude-opus-4-6-20250514",
  max_tokens: 1024,
  output_config: zodOutputFormat(schema),
  messages: [
    { role: "user", content: "Extract: John is 30, john@example.com" },
  ],
});

// Parse guaranteed valid output
const result = JSON.parse(response.content[0].text);
```

## Key Guarantees

✅ **Claude will only output valid JSON** matching your schema  
✅ **No hallucinated fields** — `additionalProperties: false` blocks extras  
✅ **All required fields present** — enforced by schema validation  
✅ **Type checking enforced** — integers stay integers, strings stay strings  
✅ **If schema can't be satisfied**, Claude refuses with an error (won't approximate)

## Schema Constraints

- **Max 20 strict tools** or **one JSON schema** per request
- **Max 24 optional parameters** in the schema
- Schema must be valid JSON Schema (subset of JSON Schema Draft 7)

## With Vision & Images

Combine with image analysis for guaranteed structured extraction:

```python
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6-20250514",
    max_tokens=1024,
    output_config={
        "format": {
            "type": "json_schema",
            "schema": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "items": {
                        "type": "array",
                        "items": {
                            "type": "object",
                            "properties": {
                                "name": {"type": "string"},
                                "price": {"type": "number"}
                            },
                            "required": ["name", "price"]
                        }
                    }
                },
                "required": ["items"]
            }
        }
    },
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": [
                {"type": "text", "text": "Extract all products from this receipt"},
                {
                    "type": "image",
                    "source": {
                        "type": "base64",
                        "media_type": "image/jpeg",
                        "data": "<base64_image_data>"
                    }
                }
            ]
        }
    ]
)
```

## Also Works With Tools

Pair with structured **tool use** for guaranteed correct function calls:

```python
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6-20250514",
    max_tokens=1024,
    tools=[
        {
            "type": "function",
            "function": {
                "name": "create_user",
                "strict": True,  # ← Guarantees tool inputs match schema
                "parameters": {
                    "type": "object",
                    "properties": {
                        "name": {"type": "string"},
                        "email": {"type": "string"}
                    },
                    "required": ["name", "email"]
                }
            }
        }
    ],
    messages=[{"role": "user", "content": "Create user John, john@example.com"}]
)
```

## Which Models Support This?

- ✅ Opus 4.6, Sonnet 4.6, Haiku 4.5
- ✅ All platforms (Claude.ai, Desktop, API, Bedrock, Vertex AI, Azure)
- ⚠️ **Bedrock**: Citations must be enabled for visual PDF analysis

## Avoid These Gotchas

1. **`output_format` is deprecated** — use `output_config.format` instead
2. **Schemas must be valid JSON Schema** — Claude won't accept invalid schemas
3. **No union types** (`oneOf`) — keep it simple; use `type: ["string", "number"]` for multi-type
4. **Streaming works**, but parse the full response before using structured data
5. **Use `additionalProperties: false`** if you want to block surprise fields

That's it — Claude will now guarantee valid JSON every time. 🎯

**Prompt:** I need to process an 80-page contract PDF through the API — extract key clauses, dates, and party names into structured data. What are the limits and best practices for PDF processing with Claude?

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# PDF Processing with Claude: Limits & Best Practices

## Token Budget Reality

**80 pages is feasible but requires planning:**
- A typical PDF page ≈ 500-2,000 tokens depending on density
- 80 pages ≈ 40,000-160,000 tokens (text extraction varies widely)
- Your 200k budget can handle this, but leaves limited room for follow-up queries

## Key Limits to Know

| Aspect | Limit | Notes |
|--------|-------|-------|
| File size | 20MB | Most contracts well under this |
| Image quality | Works OK | OCR capable but not perfect for scanned PDFs |
| Single request context | 200k tokens | Your entire budget per message |
| Response tokens | Variable | Model generates output from remaining budget |

## Recommended Approach

### 1. **Preprocess Before API Call**
```python
# Extract text using PDF library first
from PyPDF2 import PdfReader

reader = PdfReader("contract.pdf")
text = ""
for page in reader.pages:
    text += page.extract_text()
```

**Why:** Removes overhead, gives you control over text quality and allows token counting before submitting.

### 2. **Structured Extraction Prompt**

```python
prompt = """Extract from this contract:
1. Party names (buyer, seller, service provider, etc.)
2. Key dates (signature, effective, termination, renewal)
3. Major clauses: payment terms, confidentiality, liability, termination conditions
4. Any special conditions or obligations

Format as JSON with these keys:
- parties: [{name, role}, ...]
- dates: [{description, date}, ...]
- clauses: [{name, summary}, ...]
- obligations: [...]

Contract text:
[CONTRACT TEXT HERE]
"""
```

### 3. **Handle Large Documents**

**Option A: Chunking (if necessary)**
- Split into sections (recitals, terms, schedules)
- Process each with shared context about earlier sections
- Consolidate results

**Option B: Direct submission (simpler)**
- If 80 pages fits your token budget comfortably
- More consistent extraction than chunking
- More cost-effective (fewer API calls)

## Best Practices

✅ **DO:**
- Use vision capabilities for scanned PDFs (auto-OCR)
- Request JSON output for easier parsing
- Ask for confidence levels on uncertain fields
- Specify handling of amendments/schedules
- Include examples of expected output format

❌ **AVOID:**
- Submitting raw PDFs to vision without text extraction attempt first
- Requesting entire clause text verbatim (summarize instead)
- Overly complex JSON schemas that confuse the model
- Assuming dates are in standard formats without verification

## Cost/Efficiency Comparison

```
Direct submission (1 call):
- 80 pages → ~80k tokens input
- Result: structured data → ~3k tokens output
- Cost: ~0.3 USD (using claude-opus or 3.5-sonnet)

Chunked approach (5-8 calls):
- Same output but multiple round-trips
- Higher total token usage
- Only needed if individual sections exceed ~100k tokens
```

## Pro Tips

1. **Add a validation step:**
   ```
   "For dates you're unsure about, return 'UNCLEAR' 
    and explain why in a confidence_note field"
   ```

2. **Handle structured data within clauses:**
   - Payment schedules → table format
   - Nested conditions → boolean logic representation

3. **Test on 2-3 pages first** to refine your prompt before the full document

4. **Keep the original PDF reference** — even with accurate extraction, you'll want page numbers to verify

## If You Hit Issues

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| Garbled text extraction | Use vision API on original PDF pages |
| Missing clauses | Add "Check schedules A-Z" reminder to prompt |
| Inconsistent formatting | Ask for multiple output formats, pick best |
| Dates in unusual formats | Provide locale/format examples in prompt |

**Bottom line:** Your 80-page contract will likely fit in a single API call. Focus on a clear extraction prompt and validate results against the original document for critical fields.

Need help with the specific extraction criteria?

# PDF Processing for Contract Analysis

Great question. Here's what you need to know for your 80-page contract:

## Limits & Capability

✅ **Your 80-page PDF is well within limits:**
- **Max per request:** 32MB, 100 pages
- **Visual layout analysis:** Supported natively (no special config)
- **All models:** PDF processing available across API, Bedrock, Vertex AI, Azure

Your contract is comfortably under the page limit. You can process it in a single request.

## Token Cost Estimation (Critical First Step)

**Before sending the PDF, estimate the cost:**

```python
import anthropic
import base64

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

with open("contract.pdf", "rb") as f:
    pdf_data = base64.standard_b64encode(f.read()).decode("utf-8")

# Estimate tokens BEFORE making the actual request
response = client.messages.count_tokens(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": [
                {
                    "type": "document",
                    "source": {
                        "type": "base64",
                        "media_type": "application/pdf",
                        "data": pdf_data,
                    },
                },
                {
                    "type": "text",
                    "text": "Extract key clauses, dates, and parties."
                }
            ],
        }
    ],
)

print(f"Input tokens: {response.input_tokens}")
print(f"Est. cost (Opus 4.6): ${response.input_tokens * 0.015 / 1_000_000:.2f}")
```

This prevents surprises. PDFs with images, scans, or complex layouts will use more tokens.

## Best Practice: Structured Outputs + PDF Processing

Use **structured outputs** (GA) to guarantee JSON:

```python
import anthropic
import json

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

# Define your extraction schema
extraction_schema = {
    "type": "object",
    "properties": {
        "parties": {
            "type": "array",
            "items": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "name": {"type": "string"},
                    "role": {"type": "string", "enum": ["buyer", "seller", "lessor", "lessee", "other"]},
                },
                "required": ["name", "role"]
            },
            "description": "All identified parties to the contract"
        },
        "key_dates": {
            "type": "array",
            "items": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "date": {"type": "string", "format": "date"},
                    "event": {"type": "string"},
                },
                "required": ["date", "event"]
            },
            "description": "Important dates: effective date, expiration, payment deadlines, etc."
        },
        "key_clauses": {
            "type": "array",
            "items": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "clause_title": {"type": "string"},
                    "summary": {"type": "string"},
                    "page_reference": {"type": "integer"},
                },
                "required": ["clause_title", "summary"]
            }
        },
        "obligations": {
            "type": "object",
            "properties": {
                "party_a_obligations": {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
                "party_b_obligations": {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
            }
        },
        "termination_clause": {"type": "string", "description": "Conditions for termination"},
        "liability_cap": {"type": "string", "description": "Any caps or limitations on liability"},
    },
    "required": ["parties", "key_dates", "key_clauses"]
}

response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=4096,
    output_config={
        "type": "json_schema",
        "json_schema": {
            "name": "ContractExtraction",
            "schema": extraction_schema,
            "strict": True
        }
    },
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": [
                {
                    "type": "document",
                    "source": {
                        "type": "base64",
                        "media_type": "application/pdf",
                        "data": pdf_data,
                    },
                },
                {
                    "type": "text",
                    "text": """You are a contract analysis expert. Extract the following from this 80-page contract:
1. All parties (names and roles)
2. Key dates (effective, expiration, payment deadlines, renewal dates)
3. Key clauses (indemnification, confidentiality, payment terms, delivery, warranties)
4. Party obligations (what each party must do)
5. Termination conditions
6. Liability caps or exclusions

Be precise. Include page references where possible. For dates, use YYYY-MM-DD format."""
                }
            ],
        }
    ],
)

# Guaranteed valid JSON
contract_data = json.loads(response.content[0].text)
print(json.dumps(contract_data, indent=2))
```

## Alternative: Use the Files API for Persistence (Beta)

If you're processing multiple PDFs or want to reuse the uploaded file:

```python
import anthropic

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

# Upload once, reference by file_id
with open("contract.pdf", "rb") as f:
    file_response = client.beta.files.upload(
        file=("contract.pdf", f, "application/pdf"),
    )

file_id = file_response.id
print(f"Uploaded file: {file_id}")

# Now reference by ID in multiple requests (no re-upload cost)
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=4096,
    betas=["files-api-2025-04-14"],
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": [
                {
                    "type": "document",
                    "source": {
                        "type": "file",
                        "file_id": file_id,
                    },
                },
                {
                    "type": "text",
                    "text": "Extract key clauses, dates, and parties from this contract."
                }
            ],
        }
    ],
)
```

**Files API benefits:**
- 500MB per file, 100GB org limit
- Reference same file in multiple requests (no re-upload)
- Persistent for the conversation

---

## Key Practices

| Practice | Why |
|----------|-----|
| **Always count tokens first** | PDFs vary widely. Scanned/image-heavy ≈ 2x more tokens than text PDFs. |
| **Use structured outputs** | Guaranteed valid JSON. No parsing errors. `strict: true` enforces schema. |
| **Use Opus 4.6 or Sonnet 4.6** | Best at complex document reasoning. For simple extraction, Haiku 4.5 works. |
| **Add context to the prompt** | Tell Claude what type of contract (purchase agreement, NDA, lease) if known. It improves accuracy. |
| **Include page references** | Helps validate extracted data and provides audit trail. |
| **Use 1M context for multiple PDFs** | If analyzing 3–5 contracts together, enable 1M context (beta header `context-1m-2025-08-07`) and load all at once. Avoids multi-step orchestration. |
| **Batch API for bulk processing** | 50% discount if processing 100+ contracts. Use `client.beta.messages.batch.create()`. |

---

## Quick Architecture Decision

**Single 80-page contract → One API call**
- Count tokens → Opus 4.6 + structured outputs
- Response: guaranteed JSON with `parties`, `dates`, `clauses`
- Cost: ~$0.02–0.05 depending on visual complexity

**Multiple contracts → Pick one:**
- **Few (2–5):** Load all

**Prompt:** I'm building a chat interface where Claude uses tools (web search, code execution). I want real-time streaming but I'm confused about how streaming works when Claude makes tool calls. How do I implement streaming with tool use?

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Streaming with Tool Use in Claude

Great question! This is more nuanced than simple text streaming. Here's how it works:

## The Key Insight

When Claude uses tools, streaming gives you **partial message deltas** that include both text and tool use blocks as they're generated. You build up the complete message incrementally.

## Implementation Flow

```python
import anthropic
import json

client = anthropic.Anthropic()

def process_tool_call(tool_name: str, tool_input: dict) -> str:
    """Mock tool execution - replace with real tools"""
    if tool_name == "web_search":
        return f"Search results for: {tool_input.get('query')}"
    elif tool_name == "code_execute":
        return f"Executed: {tool_input.get('code')}"
    return "Unknown tool"

def chat_with_streaming():
    tools = [
        {
            "name": "web_search",
            "description": "Search the web",
            "input_schema": {
                "type": "object",
                "properties": {
                    "query": {"type": "string"}
                },
                "required": ["query"]
            }
        }
    ]
    
    messages = [
        {"role": "user", "content": "What's the latest news about Claude?"}
    ]
    
    # Stream the initial response
    with client.messages.stream(
        model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
        max_tokens=4096,
        tools=tools,
        messages=messages
    ) as stream:
        # Accumulate the full message
        full_message = None
        
        for text in stream.text_stream:
            # Real-time text streaming
            print(text, end="", flush=True)
        
        # Get complete message after stream ends
        full_message = stream.get_final_message()
    
    print()  # newline
    
    # Handle tool calls if any
    if full_message.stop_reason == "tool_use":
        # Process tool calls
        tool_calls = [block for block in full_message.content 
                      if block.type == "tool_use"]
        
        for tool_call in tool_calls:
            print(f"\n🔧 Using tool: {tool_call.name}")
            print(f"   Input: {json.dumps(tool_call.input, indent=2)}")
            
            # Execute the tool
            result = process_tool_call(tool_call.name, tool_call.input)
            print(f"   Result: {result}")
            
            # Add assistant message and tool result to conversation
            messages.append({"role": "assistant", "content": full_message.content})
            messages.append({
                "role": "user",
                "content": [
                    {
                        "type": "tool_result",
                        "tool_use_id": tool_call.id,
                        "content": result
                    }
                ]
            })
        
        # Continue the conversation after tool use
        print("\n\n📝 Claude's response after tool use:")
        with client.messages.stream(
            model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
            max_tokens=4096,
            tools=tools,
            messages=messages
        ) as stream:
            for text in stream.text_stream:
                print(text, end="", flush=True)
            final = stream.get_final_message()
        
        print()
        return final
    
    return full_message

# Run it
chat_with_streaming()
```

## Web Interface (JavaScript)

```javascript
async function streamWithTools(userMessage) {
    const response = await fetch('/api/chat', {
        method: 'POST',
        headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
        body: JSON.stringify({ message: userMessage })
    });

    const reader = response.body.getReader();
    const decoder = new TextDecoder();
    
    let buffer = '';
    
    while (true) {
        const { done, value } = await reader.read();
        if (done) break;
        
        buffer += decoder.decode(value, { stream: true });
        
        // Parse streaming events
        const lines = buffer.split('\n');
        buffer = lines.pop(); // Keep incomplete line
        
        for (const line of lines) {
            if (line.startsWith('data: ')) {
                const event = JSON.parse(line.slice(6));
                
                if (event.type === 'text') {
                    // Stream text as it arrives
                    appendToChat(event.content);
                } else if (event.type === 'tool_start') {
                    // Show tool being called
                    showToolStatus(event.name, 'running');
                } else if (event.type === 'tool_result') {
                    // Show tool result
                    showToolResult(event.name, event.result);
                }
            }
        }
    }
}
```

## Backend (Flask Example)

```python
from flask import Flask, jsonify, request
import anthropic

@app.route('/api/chat', methods=['POST'])
def chat():
    user_message = request.json['message']
    
    def generate():
        messages = [{"role": "user", "content": user_message}]
        tools = [...]  # your tools
        
        with client.messages.stream(...) as stream:
            for text in stream.text_stream:
                yield f"data: {json.dumps({'type': 'text', 'content': text})}\n"
            
            message = stream.get_final_message()
        
        # Handle tool calls
        if message.stop_reason == "tool_use":
            for block in message.content:
                if block.type == "tool_use":
                    yield f"data: {json.dumps({'type': 'tool_start', 'name': block.name})}\n"
                    result = execute_tool(block.name, block.input)
                    yield f"data: {json.dumps({'type': 'tool_result', 'name': block.name, 'result': result})}\n"
                    # ... continue conversation
    
    return Response(generate(), mimetype='text/event-stream')
```

## Key Points

1. **Stream text**, then wait for complete message at stream end
2. **Check `stop_reason`** - if `"tool_use"`, extract tool calls from the complete message
3. **Execute tools** while showing real-time status to user
4. **Append results** and continue streaming for Claude's follow-up response
5. **Loop** if Claude makes multiple tool calls

The crucial difference from text-only streaming: you get *partial text* in real-time, but *complete tool call blocks* only when the stream ends.

</details>

- Completeness keywords matched: ['stop_reason', 'fine-grained', 'content_block_stop']
- Deprecated patterns found: []
