<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Browser Data Access in Claude Code

Claude Code **cannot directly access your browser cookies or browsing history**. This is by design — it's a security boundary. However, there are legitimate ways to build browsing analysis tools:

## What Claude Code *Can* Do

### 1. **Web Sessions** (Real-time browsing)
Claude Code can control your browser in real-time via:
- `claude --remote` — Start a web session and let Claude steer your browser
- `/teleport` — Pull a browser session back into Claude Code for analysis
- Slack integration (`@Claude` → auto web session)

This lets Claude *see* pages you visit and analyze them, but it's active/manual, not passive history tracking.

### 2. **Browser Automation** (CoWork)
CoWork is Claude's browser automation environment. You could:
- Write a skill or script that visits sites you specify
- Have Claude analyze pages and extract patterns
- Store results locally for trend analysis

### 3. **Manual Export + Analysis**
Most browsers let you export history:
- **Chrome**: Settings → History → History (Ctrl+H) → can export via DevTools or extensions
- **Firefox**: Bookmarks → Manage Bookmarks → can access history DB
- **Safari**: File → Export Bookmarks

Then upload the exported file to Claude Code for analysis. This gives you:
- ✅ Full control and transparency
- ✅ Privacy — data stays local until you share it
- ✅ Easy pattern analysis

### 4. **Local Data with a Skill**
Build a **Claude Code skill** that:
```bash
# Access local browser data files (if you grant permission)
sqlite3 ~/.config/google-chrome/Default/History "SELECT url, title, visit_count FROM urls ORDER BY visit_count DESC;"
```

Then call it with `/your-skill-name` to analyze the output.

---

## Why This Design?

- **Security**: Preventing automatic cookie/history access protects against malicious prompts
- **Privacy**: You explicitly choose what data to share
- **Trust**: You see exactly what Claude Code can analyze

## Recommended Approach for Your Use Case

**Build a hybrid skill:**

```yaml
# skill.yaml
name: "browse-analyzer"
description: "Analyze your browsing patterns"
```

```bash
#!/bin/bash
# Extract history from your browser's local database
# (requires explicit permission the first time)

# Chrome example (macOS/Linux)
sqlite3 ~/Library/Application\ Support/Google/Chrome/Default/History \
  "SELECT url, title, visit_count, last_visit_time FROM urls \
   ORDER BY visit_count DESC LIMIT 100;" 2>/dev/null || \
  echo "Chrome history not accessible. Please export manually."

# Firefox example
sqlite3 ~/.mozilla/firefox/*/places.sqlite \
  "SELECT url, title, visit_count FROM moz_places \
   ORDER BY visit_count DESC LIMIT 100;" 2>/dev/null || \
  echo "Firefox history not accessible. Please export manually."
```

Then in Claude Code:
```
/browse-analyzer
```

Claude analyzes the output and gives you insights (top domains, patterns by time, category clustering, etc.).

---

## Bottom Line

| Method | Setup | Privacy | Real-time |
|--------|-------|---------|-----------|
| Web sessions (`--remote`) | Built-in | ✅ (you steer) | ✅ |
| Manual export | One-time | ✅ (you control) | ❌ |
| Local skill | One-time | ✅ (filesystem only) | ✅ |
| Browser extension* | Install | ⚠️ (third-party) | ✅ |

\* *Requires a separate browser extension (not Claude); Claude can't install it.*

**Start with**: Export your history as CSV/JSON from your browser, then ask Claude Code to analyze the file. Zero setup, full transparency, same insights.

</details>

- Stores facts Claude learns about you
- Persists across conversations via your app's storage

- Your goals or constraints

# Internet Access & HTTP Requests

Claude **cannot** access the internet or make HTTP requests by default. However, there are several ways to enable this depending on your platform:

## Available Options

### 1. **Web Search & Web Fetch Tools (API)**
Claude can fetch live data from URLs using built-in tools:

```python
client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4.6",
    max_tokens=1024,
    tools=[
        {"type": "web_fetch_20260209", "name": "web_fetch"}
    ],
    messages=[{
        "role": "user",
        "content": "Fetch data from my API at https://api.example.com/data"
    }]
)
```

**Limitations:**
- Only **GET requests** (no POST, PUT, DELETE)
- No authentication headers by default
- Primarily designed for public web content

### 2. **Code Execution Tool (Best for APIs)**
Enable code execution to call your REST API with full control:

```python
client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4.6",
    max_tokens=1024,
    tools=[
        {"type": "code_execution_20260120", "name": "code_execution"}
    ],
    messages=[{
        "role": "user",
        "content": "Call my API at https://api.example.com/users with authentication"
    }]
)
```

Claude can write Python code to:
- Make any HTTP method (GET, POST, PUT, DELETE)
- Add custom headers and authentication
- Parse JSON responses
- Process the data

### 3. **MCP (Model Context Protocol) - Most Robust**
For production integrations, use MCP to connect directly to your service:

**Via MCP Connector (API):**
```python
client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4.6",
    max_tokens=1024,
    tools=[
        {"type": "mcp_client_20251120", ...}
    ],
    messages=[...]
)
```

**Via Claude Code (CLI):**
Set up an MCP server that wraps your API, then Claude has structured access with validation, error handling, and rate limiting built-in.

### 4. **Claude Code / Desktop + MCP**
If using Claude Code or Desktop, you can:
- Install an MCP server for your API
- Create a **Skill** that calls your API via code execution
- Set up **Hooks** for automatic requests after certain events

## Recommendation for Your Use Case

For pulling live data from your REST API:

| Scenario | Best Choice |
|----------|-------------|
| Simple public API (no auth) | Web Fetch tool |
| API with authentication | Code Execution tool |
| Production service integration | MCP server |
| Recurring data pulls | Claude Code + `/loop` or background task |
| Team automation | Claude Code + Plugin (bundles skills + hooks) |

**Most straightforward approach:**
```python
tools=[
    {"type": "code_execution_20260120", "name": "code_execution"}
]
```

Then Claude can write:
```python
import requests

response = requests.get(
    'https://api.example.com/data',
    headers={'Authorization': 'Bearer YOUR_TOKEN'}
)
data = response.json()
# Process data...
```

## Key Limitations

- **No persistent network access** — each request starts fresh
- **Sandboxed execution** — code runs in an isolated container (safe, but can't access your local network)
- **Stateless by default** — use the Memory tool or Files API for persistence across conversations
- **Rate limiting** — your API should handle rapid requests from code execution

For details on configuration and examples, see `references/tool-types.md` and `references/api-features.md` in the full documentation.

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

I need to clarify what Claude can actually do with code execution.

**Claude can execute code, but with limitations:**

Claude has access to a **code execution environment** (via the `code_execution` tool), but it's **not a general-purpose compiler/runtime for all languages**. Here's what you should know:

## What Claude Can Do

- **Python** — Full support, including pip package installation
- **JavaScript/Node.js** — Supported
- **Bash/shell scripting** — Supported
- **Limited other languages** — Some basic support, but not comprehensive

## What Claude Cannot Reliably Do

**Rust compilation is not supported.** You cannot ask Claude to compile and run Rust code directly via the code execution environment. The sandbox doesn't include a Rust compiler or the necessary build toolchain.

## What You *Can* Do Instead

1. **Write Rust code for you to compile locally** — Claude can write correct, working Rust code; you just run it on your machine.

2. **Use Python to interact with Rust** — Claude can execute Python that calls compiled Rust binaries (if they're available in the environment).

3. **Use alternative languages** — If you need Claude to actually *execute* compiled code, stick with Python or JavaScript.

4. **Leverage web APIs** — If there's an online Rust playground or service, Claude can fetch results via web tools.

## Bottom Line

Claude is excellent at **writing** Rust code, but if you need **execution and testing**, you'll need to run it yourself or use a language Claude's sandbox actually supports (Python, Node.js, Bash). For compiled languages like Rust, C++, Go, Claude's strength is in code generation and explanation, not live execution.

</details>

# Sonnet 3.7 Migration Guide

**Sonnet 3.7 is retired as of February 2026.** You need to migrate immediately.

## What to Move To

Your best options depend on your use case:

| If you need... | Move to | Why |
|---|---|---|
| Drop-in replacement | **Sonnet 4.6** | Same cost tier, much better performance, adaptive thinking support |
| Maximum quality | **Opus 4.6** | Best reasoning, 200K→1M context (beta), 128K output tokens |
| Cost optimization | **Haiku 4.5** | $1/$5 pricing, still strong for classification/routing tasks |

### Recommended: Sonnet 4.6

- **Cost**: $3/$15 per MTok (same as 3.7)
- **Performance**: Significantly better across reasoning, coding, and multimodal tasks
- **New capabilities**: Adaptive thinking, 1M context (beta), 64K output
- **Backward compatibility**: Works as a drop-in replacement — just update the model ID

**Model ID**: `claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022`

---

## Migration Steps

### 1. **Update your model ID**
```python
# Old
client.messages.create(model="claude-3-7-sonnet", ...)

# New
client.messages.create(model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022", ...)
```

### 2. **Test your prompts**
Sonnet 4.6 is more capable, so:
- Prompts that worked with 3.7 will work better (often with no changes)
- If you have very tight temperature/instructions, validate outputs
- Run a quick A/B test on a sample of your workload

### 3. **Optional: Add adaptive thinking** (if you want better reasoning)
```python
client.messages.create(
    model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
    thinking={"type": "adaptive"},  # New in 4.6
    messages=[...]
)
```

### 4. **Optional: Use 1M context** (if you hit 200K limits)
```python
client.messages.create(
    model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
    messages=[...],
    betas=["context-1m-2025-08-07"]  # Requires Tier 3+ org
)
```

---

- **Sonnet 3.7**: Retired Feb 2026 (now)
- **Haiku 3**: Retiring April 2026 — if you use Haiku 3, migrate to **Haiku 4.5** soon
- **Sonnet 4.5**: Still available but use 4.6 (better)
- **Opus 4.5**: Still available but use 4.6 (better)

---

**Good news**: Sonnet 4.6 has the same pricing as 3.7, so no bill shock. If anything, you might spend *less* because:
- Better quality = fewer retries
- Adaptive thinking is efficient (you pay only for thinking tokens, not output)

---

- **"My prompts are highly tuned to 3.7"** → Test first, but expect improvements. Sonnet 4.6 is more capable, not just different.

- **"We use Bedrock/Vertex"** → Check your provider's model availability; they may lag. Fall back to Sonnet 4.5 if needed.

# Automated Tasks on Claude Desktop

I have good news and some limitations to be aware of.

## What's NOT Available on Desktop

Claude Desktop **does not support**:
- **Hooks** (deterministic automation after file edits/commits)
- **Background tasks** (`Ctrl+B`)
- **Cron/scheduling** (`/loop`, recurring timers)
- **Code execution** (required for many automation patterns)

These are **Claude Code features only** — they're built into the CLI and IDE extensions, not the Desktop app.

## What IS Available on Desktop

You can use **Skills** for repeatable workflows, but they require manual invocation:
- Create a skill that runs linting checks
- Invoke it with `/skill-name` or by describing what you need
- It won't trigger automatically

For persistent context across sessions, **Projects** help you maintain setup, but again—no automatic execution.

---

## Your Best Path Forward

**Switch to Claude Code** if you need true automation. It's purpose-built for this:

### Example Setup in Claude Code

**Hook for linting on every edit:**
```yaml
hooks:
  - type: "shell"
    trigger: "after_file_edit"
    command: "npm run lint -- {{file}}"
```

**Background task for monitoring every 5 minutes:**
```bash
/loop every 5 minutes
run: curl https://your-service/health && echo "Service is up" || echo "Service is down"
```

**Why Claude Code works here:**
- Hooks run *without* token cost (deterministic shell commands)
- `/loop` scheduling handles recurring tasks efficiently
- Code execution is built-in and free when paired with other tools
- You keep your development workflow (VS Code, JetBrains, CLI)

---

## If You're Committed to Desktop

You'd need **external automation** (not Claude):
- Use your OS's native task scheduler (cron on Mac/Linux, Task Scheduler on Windows) to call linting scripts
- Set up service monitoring with a separate tool (Datadog, Prometheus, etc.)
- Claude Desktop stays focused on interactive work

---

## My Recommendation

If automated linting and monitoring are core to your workflow, **Claude Code is the right choice**. It's designed exactly for this use case and keeps everything in one place. You get the same Claude intelligence you're used to on Desktop, plus automation superpowers.

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

On **Claude.ai**, skills are **auto-invoked based on natural language context** — there's no slash command syntax like you might have on Claude Code.

Here's how it works:

## Auto-Invocation (Claude.ai)

When you ask Claude about a topic related to your skill, it automatically detects the skill is relevant and uses it. For example:
- If your skill teaches Claude how to analyze financial documents, just ask: *"Can you analyze this spreadsheet?"*
- Claude recognizes the skill applies and invokes it automatically.

There's **no direct `/skillname` trigger** on Claude.ai (unlike Claude Code, which supports `/simplify`, `/batch`, etc.).

## If Direct Invocation Isn't Triggering

If your skill isn't auto-invoking when it should:

1. **Be explicit in your prompt** — mention the topic/domain the skill covers:
   - Instead of: "Help me"
   - Try: "Using [skill topic], help me with..."

2. **Check the skill's context** — Your ZIP skill includes documentation that Claude reads. Make sure the skill's README or metadata clearly describes what it does.

3. **Consider the problem domain** — If the skill teaches a niche technique, Claude might not always recognize it's relevant. Explicitly asking Claude to "use my [skill name] skill" can help prompt recognition.

## Better Control? Try Claude Code

If you need **direct slash command invocation** (`/myskill`) or more control over when a skill runs, **Claude Code** is the better fit:
- Full `/skillname` syntax support
- Deterministic invocation via hooks
- Scheduled execution (`/loop`)
- Better for workflows requiring precise triggering

For Claude.ai, the design is intentionally about context-aware auto-invocation — Claude learns what your skill does and uses it when relevant.

### Test 8.3: Cross-Platform Awareness

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Better Approaches for Storing Coding Standards

Yes, pasting into the system prompt each time isn't ideal. Here are better options:

## 1. **Files API** (Best for large documents)
- Upload your style guide as a file that Claude can reference
- Reduces token usage vs. embedding in every system prompt
- Good for comprehensive guides, examples, templates
- Trade-off: Slightly slower than having it in system context

```python
# Pseudocode
with open("style_guide.md", "rb") as f:
    response = client.beta.messages.create(
        model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
        max_tokens=1024,
        system="Follow the coding standards in the provided file.",
        messages=[
            {
                "role": "user",
                "content": [
                    {
                        "type": "document",
                        "source": {
                            "type": "file",
                            "file_id": file_id
                        }
                    },
                    {"type": "text", "text": "Review this code..."}
                ]
            }
        ]
    )
```

## 2. **Cached System Prompt** (Best for consistency + efficiency)
- Store standards in system prompt with prompt caching enabled
- Tokens are cached after first use, dramatically reducing costs
- Best if your standards don't change frequently

## 3. **Hybrid Approach** (Recommended)
- Put core standards in a cached system prompt
- Use Files API for supplementary examples/edge cases
- Balances speed, cost, and flexibility

## Key Consideration
If your standards change often, the Files API keeps you more flexible. If they're stable, prompt caching saves the most money over time.

What's your typical use case—code review, generation, or something else?

</details>

#### Treatment Response
- Accuracy keywords matched: ['system prompt', 'claude.md', 'project', 'prompt caching']
- Completeness keywords matched: ['claude code', 'claude.ai', 'persistent', 'reference file']
- Deprecated patterns found: []
- Judge — Accuracy: 2, Completeness: 3, Actionability: 2

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

Yes! You have several better options depending on your use case:

## Best Options for Your Situation

**1. Prompt Caching (Recommended for API)**
If you're using the Claude API directly, enable **prompt caching** on your system prompt:

```python
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=1024,
    system=[
        {
            "type": "text",
            "text": YOUR_CODING_STANDARDS,
            "cache_control": {"type": "ephemeral"}
        }
    ],
    messages=[{"role": "user", "content": "Review this code..."}]
)
```

This caches your standards for 5 minutes across requests, reducing both latency and costs (you pay 10% of the cached tokens on reads instead of the full amount). Perfect if your standards don't change frequently.

**2. Memory Tool (For Long-Running Apps)**
If you're building a custom application where Claude needs to *persist* context across conversations, use the **Memory tool**:

```python
tools = [{"type": "memory_20250818", "name": "memory"}]
```

Claude can autonomously save critical standards and retrieve them later. Requires client-side storage but ideal for stateful applications.

**3. Files API (For Large Documents)**
If your standards are extensive (>100KB), use the **Files API** to upload once and reference:

```python
file_response = client.beta.files.upload(
    file=open("coding_standards.pdf", "rb"),
)
# Then reference file_id in messages
```

Upload once, reuse the file ID across many requests. Works well with 1M context.

## Platform-Specific Alternatives

- **Claude.ai or Desktop**: Use **Projects** to create a persistent project for your standards. Claude loads that context automatically for all conversations in that project.
- **Claude Code** (if using it): Store standards in **CLAUDE.md** (~200 lines) or overflow to **`.claude/rules/`** files. This loads automatically in every session.

## Quick Comparison

| Approach | Best For | Cost | Setup |
|----------|----------|------|-------|
| **Prompt caching** | Frequent API calls, <5 min cache window | 90% savings on cached reads | Simple, no extra storage |
| **Memory tool** | Multi-turn apps, evolving standards | Normal usage | Client-side storage needed |
| **Files API** | Large documents (>100KB) | Normal usage | One upload, many uses |
| **Projects** | Claude.ai/Desktop workflows | Free (built-in) | Create project, upload once |

**My recommendation**: Start with **prompt caching** on your system prompt—it's the simplest for API-based products and gives immediate cost savings. If you need persistent updates or evolving standards across conversations, layer in the **Memory tool**.

</details>

Great question! Your colleague is using two Claude.ai features that work differently in Claude Code. Let me break them down:

## Projects (Persistent Document Context)

**On Claude.ai:** Projects let you upload documents once, then Claude automatically references them across all conversations in that project. It's like a persistent knowledge base for that specific project.

**In Claude Code:** Projects don't exist as a built-in feature, but you can achieve the same thing using **CLAUDE.md**:

- Create a `CLAUDE.md` file in your project root (Claude Code always loads and reads it)
- Store document summaries, key information, or even embed content there (~200 lines max)
- For overflow, use `.claude/rules/` for additional files
- This persists across all Claude Code conversations in that workspace

**Alternative:** If you need full document management like Claude.ai, you could:
- Use the **Files API** (beta) to upload documents programmatically
- Store file IDs in your CLAUDE.md or a `.claude/` config file
- Reference them in requests

## Interactive Widgets (MCP Apps)

**On Claude.ai:** The "interactive widget" is likely an **MCP App** — a beta feature where Claude creates an interactive HTML UI that runs within Claude.ai.

**In Claude Code:** You have *more* powerful options:
- **Skills** — create reusable workflows/tools (similar to Claude.ai)
- **Plugins** — bundle skills, hooks, and MCP together for distribution
- **MCP servers** — connect to external services (full support via stdio/HTTP/SSE)
- **Code execution** — Claude can run Python/Bash directly without a separate app
- **Hooks** — automate tasks deterministically (shell or HTTP)

The closest equivalent to an "interactive widget" would be:
1. **A skill with embedded UI** — craft a skill that generates HTML/interactive output
2. **MCP with a web UI** — build an MCP server that serves a web interface
3. **Direct code execution** — Claude generates and runs Python that produces interactive output

## Quick Comparison

| Feature | Claude.ai | Claude Code |
|---------|-----------|------------|
| **Persistent docs** | Projects | CLAUDE.md + .claude/rules/ |
| **Interactive UI** | MCP Apps (beta) | Skills, code execution, MCP servers, hooks |
| **Reusable workflows** | Saved threads | Skills (filesystem or `skills.sh` registry) |
| **External integrations** | Limited | Full MCP support (stdio/HTTP/SSE) |

## Recommendation for Your Workflow

Since you use Claude Code daily in the terminal:

1. **For document persistence:** Create a `CLAUDE.md` at your project root with key context
2. **For interactive tools:** Write a **skill** (it can generate HTML/CLI output) or use **code execution** to create dynamic outputs
3. **For external services:** Set up **MCP servers** if you need runtime integrations

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Key Differences: CoWork vs Claude Code

You're asking about genuinely different product tiers. Here's what you're missing:

## **CoWork Limitations**
- **No subagents**: You can't spawn autonomous child agents to handle parallel tasks or delegated work
- **No hooks**: Can't set up event-driven automation (e.g., "when X happens, trigger Y")
- **No agent teams**: Can't orchestrate multiple specialized agents working together on complex workflows
- **Plugin-based extensibility**: Limited to what's available as plugins vs. programmatic control

## **Claude Code Advantages**
- **Subagents**: Create specialized mini-agents for specific tasks, with the parent agent delegating and coordinating
- **Hooks**: Event triggers that connect to external systems (webhooks, scheduled tasks, real-time events)
- **Agent teams**: Multiple agents with different capabilities working in concert on complex problems
- **Native code execution**: More direct control over agent behavior vs. plugin constraints

## **The Real Gap**

The difference isn't just feature count—it's **architectural**:
- **CoWork** = Claude + tools (plugins/MCP)
- **Claude Code** = Agentic orchestration layer where agents can manage other agents and respond to events

## **Should You Switch?**

Ask yourself:
1. Do you need **parallel agent execution** or **delegation patterns**?
2. Do you need **event-driven automation** beyond manual triggers?
3. Would **specialized sub-agents** meaningfully reduce complexity?

If you're mostly using Claude as a smart assistant with plugin calls, CoWork is sufficient. If you're building multi-step orchestration or need true agent autonomy, Claude Code is the gap you're feeling.

What's your main workflow looking like?

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# CoWork vs Claude Code: What You're Missing

You're on a solid foundation with CoWork—skills and MCP via plugins cover a lot. But Claude Code does unlock some powerful multi-agent and automation capabilities that CoWork doesn't have. Here's the honest breakdown:

## Features CoWork Lacks

| Feature | What It Does | Impact on Your Workflow |
|---------|-------------|------------------------|
| **Subagents** | Isolated workers with their own system prompts & tool sets | Can't partition complex tasks—everything runs in one context window |
| **Agent Teams** | Coordinate multiple subagents in parallel | No built-in orchestration for concurrent work |
| **Hooks** | Deterministic automation (shell/HTTP) on file changes, commits, etc. | Manual triggers only; no "run X after every edit" automation |
| **Background Tasks** (`Ctrl+B`) | Long-running processes, polling, monitoring | No persistent background work |
| **/loop** & Cron | Scheduled or repeating automation | Can't set up recurring checks/refreshes |
| **Code Review** | Managed PR review service (Teams/Enterprise) | Manual reviews or external tooling |
| **Remote Control** (`/rc`) | Continue sessions from phone/browser | Stuck at your primary workstation |
| **Web Sessions** (`--remote`, `/teleport`) | Spawn controlled browser tabs, pull them back | Limited browser automation; CoWork has it but as a separate environment |

## When You'd Notice the Gap

**Subagents & Teams** are most painful if you're doing:
- **Multi-step document processing** → need different Claude instances to process different docs in parallel
- **Complex workflows** with multiple sequential stages → want each stage to have a focused prompt + specific tools
- **Role-based collaboration** → e.g., "researcher subagent" gathers data, "analyst subagent" interprets, "writer subagent" composes

**Hooks** hurt if you have:
- CI/CD pipelines where Claude should auto-review code on every commit
- Monitoring tasks ("check this endpoint every 5 minutes")
- File watchers ("process uploads automatically")

**Code Review** is Enterprise/Teams only, but if you do manage it, it's much faster than manual Claude review in CoWork.

## What CoWork Still Does Well

You're **not** missing out on:
- **Skills** — Auto-invoke from natural language ✓ (same as Claude Code)
- **MCP** — Full service connections ✓ (via plugins, like Claude Code)
- **Vision, web search, code execution** — All available ✓
- **Structured outputs** — Works in CoWork ✓
- **Large contexts (200K+)** — Supported ✓

CoWork is genuinely sufficient for single-agent workflows—research, document analysis, content creation, web browsing, etc.

## Practical Migration Path

If your team is considering the switch, here's what to evaluate:

1. **Do you need parallel task execution?**
   - No → Stay on CoWork
   - Yes → Subagents would unlock this

2. **Do you have deterministic automation (CI/CD, file watchers)?**
   - No → CoWork is fine
   - Yes → Hooks would save engineering overhead

3. **Are you running long background processes?**
   - No → CoWork is fine
   - Yes → `/loop` and background tasks help

4. **Do you manage code reviews at scale?**
   - No/Manually → CoWork is fine
   - Yes & Enterprise tier → Code Review service is valuable

## Bottom Line

**Stay on CoWork if:**
- Your workflows are primarily single-agent (one Claude instance doing the work)
- Automation is event-driven, not time-based
- You don't need parallel execution

**Consider Claude Code if:**
- You're building multi-step systems where different stages need different prompts/tools
- You have CI/CD or monitoring tasks
- Your team is on Enterprise/Teams and wants managed Code Review

CoWork + plugins is a fully capable platform—don't feel pressured to migrate unless you hit one of those constraints. The features you're missing are real, but they're architectural rather than capability-level. You can often work around them by engineering at the API level (orchestrating multiple Claude calls yourself), but at that point, Claude Code's subagents become more cost-effective.

Want help evaluating a specific workflow to see if CoWork is the blocker?

</details>

# Claude's Integration Capabilities

You're right to explore options—Claude **cannot natively connect** to external services on its own, but the path forward depends on your use case.

## What Claude Can't Do
- Direct API calls to Slack, GitHub, databases, etc.
- Persistent connections or real-time monitoring
- Store credentials securely
- Execute code that persists or triggers actions

## Where You *Can* Build Integrations

**1. Claude API + Your Own Backend (Best for production)**
- Use the Claude API in your application code
- Your backend handles auth, API calls, data management
- You control everything; Claude is just the AI engine
- Works with any tech stack

**2. Claude with Tools/Function Calling**
- Define custom functions your backend exposes
- Claude can "call" them and you execute them server-side
- Example: Claude tells your backend "fetch GitHub repo X"

**3. Make.com, Zapier, N8N (No-code/low-code)**
- Build workflows that call Claude API + other services
- Easier setup but less flexible
- Good for simple automation

## Why Your Current Attempts Won't Work

- **Claude.ai**: No integration features, just chat
- **Desktop**: Same limitations as web version
- **Claude Code**: Can generate code but can't execute external API calls

## Quick Decision Tree

- **"I want to build an app"** → Claude API + your backend
- **"I need simple automation"** → Make.com/Zapier
- **"I want AI to help write code"** → Use Claude to generate boilerplate, then integrate yourself

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Connecting Claude to External Services

Yes, Claude can connect to external services, but **the platform you choose dramatically affects what's possible**. Let me break down your options:

## Platform Comparison for External Integrations

| Service Type | Claude.ai | Desktop | Claude Code | Best Choice |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Slack** | MCP Connectors | MCP via Settings | Full MCP + native Slack hook | **Claude Code** |
| **GitHub** | MCP Connectors | MCP via Settings | Full MCP + native Git integration | **Claude Code** |
| **Databases** | MCP Connectors | MCP via Settings | Full MCP + code execution | **Claude Code** |
| **Custom APIs** | Limited | Limited | Full MCP + HTTP hooks | **Claude Code** |

**Bottom line:** If you need reliable, production-grade external service integration, **Claude Code is the right choice**. Claude.ai and Desktop are better for one-off tasks or simple integrations.

---

## How Each Platform Connects to Services

### Claude.ai & Desktop (Limited)
- **MCP Connectors**: Can connect to pre-built MCP servers, but setup is GUI-based and limited to what Anthropic has pre-configured
- **No native hooks**: Can't automatically trigger on GitHub commits, Slack messages, etc.
- **No code execution**: Can't run database queries or custom API logic directly
- **Use case**: Quick integrations with popular services (if available as a connector)

### Claude Code (Full Power)
**This is where external service integration gets serious:**

1. **MCP (Model Context Protocol)** — Connect to any external service:
   - Slack, GitHub, databases, custom APIs
   - Can run **stdio**, **HTTP**, or **SSE** MCP servers
   - Multiple servers per request
   - Example: `npm install -g @modelcontextprotocol/server-github` → Claude has GitHub access

2. **HTTP Hooks** — Trigger Claude workflows on external events:
   ```
   POST /message → GitHub push detected → Claude Code auto-runs review
   ```
   
3. **Code Execution** — Run Python/Node directly:
   - Query databases (PostgreSQL, MongoDB, etc.)
   - Call custom APIs
   - Process responses and take action

4. **Slack Integration** — @Claude mentions auto-launch Code sessions:
   ```
   @Claude review this PR → Code runs, posts results back to Slack
   ```

5. **Background Tasks** (`Ctrl+B`)** — Monitor services continuously:
   - Poll GitHub for new PRs
   - Watch database for changes
   - Send periodic Slack updates

---

## Concrete Example: GitHub + Slack + Database

Here's what **Claude Code** can do that others can't:

```yaml
Setup:
1. MCP Server (Stdio) → GitHub API access
2. MCP Server (Stdio) → Database connection
3. HTTP Hook → Listen for GitHub push events
4. Slack integration → Post results to channel

Workflow:
User pushes code to GitHub
  ↓
HTTP hook triggers Claude Code
  ↓
Claude uses MCP to fetch:
   • Changed files (GitHub)
   • Test coverage metrics (database)
  ↓
Runs code execution to analyze
  ↓
Posts summary to Slack
```

**Claude.ai can't do this** because it lacks code execution and HTTP hooks.

---

## How to Set Up Each Service

### Slack (Claude Code)
1. Install the Slack MCP server:
   ```bash
   npm install -g @modelcontextprotocol/server-slack
   ```
2. Configure in Claude Code settings → MCP → add Slack server
3. Use `/teleport` to run from Slack or set up HTTP hook for incoming messages

### GitHub (Claude Code)
1. Install GitHub MCP server:
   ```bash
   npm install -g @modelcontextprotocol/server-github
   ```
2. Add GitHub PAT to environment
3. Set up HTTP hook to trigger on push/PR events, or use `/loop` for polling

### Databases (Claude Code)
1. Install DB MCP server (e.g., PostgreSQL):
   ```bash
   npm install -g @modelcontextprotocol/server-postgres
   ```
2. Configure connection string in environment
3. Use code execution + MCP to query and analyze data

### Custom APIs (Claude Code)
- Use **HTTP hooks** to accept webhooks from your services
- Claude Code can call any REST API via code execution
- Combine with MCP for persistent connections

---

## Quick Decision Tree

**Choose Claude.ai/Desktop if:**
- You just want to ask Claude about Slack/GitHub occasionally
- You need a simple one-off integration (no automation)
- You want the simplest setup with minimal configuration

**Choose Claude Code if:**
- ✅ You need **automated workflows** (e.g., PR review on every push)
- ✅ You need **bidirectional sync** (Claude reads AND writes to services)
- ✅ You need **background monitoring** (continuous checking)
- ✅ You need **custom business logic** (databases, APIs, transformations)
- ✅ You need **Slack integration** (auto-launch from mentions)
- ✅ You need **deterministic automation** (hooks, not just AI reasoning)

---

Since you've tried Claude.ai, Desktop, and Code, here's what each platform can't do:

| Limitation | Claude.ai | Desktop | Claude Code |
|---|---|---|---|
| Run webhooks | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |
| Query databases | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |

| Slack auto-launch | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |

| Code Review (managed) | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |

# Options for Persistent Preferences in Claude Desktop

You have two strong options, each suited to different needs:

## 1. **Projects** (Recommended for most use cases)

This is the native solution built into Claude Desktop specifically for persistent context.

**How it works:**
- Create a Project for each major area (e.g., "MyStartup Backend", "Personal Scripts")
- Add your preferences, style guides, framework details, and project context as files or text within the project
- Every conversation in that project automatically includes this context
- Switch between projects depending on what you're working on

**What to include:**
```
Project: "My Coding Setup"
├── Coding style guide (naming conventions, formatting, patterns you prefer)
├── Framework versions & preferred packages (React 18, Next.js 14, etc.)
├── Project-specific names (API endpoints, component naming patterns)
├── Common imports or boilerplate
└── Team/org context if applicable
```

**Pros:**
- ✅ Zero setup — native to Claude Desktop
- ✅ Automatic inclusion in every message (no manual work)
- ✅ Works across all conversations within a project
- ✅ Easy to switch contexts (just pick a different project)

**Cons:**
- ⚠️ Need to create separate projects for different contexts
- ⚠️ Not ideal if you work across many fragmented contexts

---

## 2. **Skills** (For reusable workflows)

If your preferences are tied to *actions* you take repeatedly, package them as a skill.

**How it works:**
- Create a ZIP file containing instructions for your coding style
- Upload via Desktop Settings > Capabilities > Skills
- Claude auto-invokes the skill when relevant, or you trigger it manually

**When to use this:**
- "Every time I write React components, follow my style guide"
- "Always structure API responses like this"
- "My preferred folder layout is..."

**Pros:**
- ✅ Reusable across projects
- ✅ Can be shared with teammates
- ✅ Auto-invocation based on context

**Cons:**
- ⚠️ Requires packaging/setup
- ⚠️ Not ideal for large amounts of reference material

---

## Recommendation

**Start with Projects.** For each major context you work in:

1. Create a project in Claude Desktop
2. Add a document with your preferences:
   - Coding conventions (naming, formatting, structure)
   - Framework/tool versions
   - Project-specific terminology
   - Any reusable snippets

Then within that project, all conversations will "remember" these preferences automatically.

**If you discover repeated patterns** (e.g., "I always format APIs this way" or "I always use these 5 imports"), *then* consider packaging that as a Skill for reuse across projects.

This gives you the persistence you want without managing separate tools or configuration files.

</details>

# Claude Customization & Extension: Complete Picture

## 1. Claude.ai (Web Interface)

### Built-in Features
- **Custom Instructions** - Set persistent preferences for how Claude responds (tone, format, constraints)
- **Projects** - Organize conversations and shared context within a workspace
- **Artifacts** - Separate code/content rendering for cleaner interaction
- **File uploads** - Share documents, images, code for analysis
- **Web search** - Real-time information retrieval

### What you *cannot* do
- No custom models or fine-tuning
- No persistent system prompts beyond custom instructions
- No integration with external APIs/tools from the interface itself

**Best for:** Ad-hoc brainstorming, testing ideas, quick analysis

---

## 2. Claude Code (Development Environment)

This appears to be a specialized interface (claude.ai for coding-focused work), but doesn't have unique customization beyond Claude.ai.

**Key difference:** Optimized workspace for code generation, debugging, and file management, but uses the same underlying API and customization options as Claude.ai.

---

## 3. Claude API (Programmatic Access)

This is where real customization lives. Multiple approaches:

### A. System Prompts & Instructions
```
messages=[
  {"role": "user", "content": "..."}
],
system="You are an expert in X. Always respond in Y format."
```
- Persistent behavior definition
- Applied to every request
- Far more flexible than web UI custom instructions

### B. Prompt Caching
- Store long context (system prompts, documents, examples) to:
  - Reduce API costs (90% discount on cached tokens)
  - Speed up repetitive requests
  - Ideal for RAG systems and multi-turn workflows

### C. Vision Capabilities
- Analyze images, diagrams, screenshots
- Extract text, understand layout
- Integrated via base64 or URLs

### D. Function Calling / Tool Use
- Define custom tools Claude can invoke
- Claude reasons about *when* to use them
- You handle execution, return results
- Examples: database queries, API calls, calculations

```python
tools=[
  {
    "name": "search_database",
    "description": "...",
    "input_schema": {...}
  }
]
```

### E. Batch Processing API
- Submit multiple requests at once
- 50% cost reduction
- Process asynchronously
- Perfect for non-urgent bulk work

### F. Multimodal Input
- Text, images, documents
- Video frames (via image sequences)
- Audio transcription (bring your own)

---

## 4. Partnerships & Integrations (Coming/Available)

### Claude for Enterprise
- Higher rate limits
- Volume pricing
- Dedicated support
- Custom SLAs

### Third-party Integrations
Claude is available through:
- **LangChain** - Framework for building with LLMs
- **Zapier** - No-code automation
- **Anthropic's partners** - Expanding ecosystem

*(Note: No native fine-tuning available yet—this is a key difference from some competitors)*

---

| Feature | Claude.ai | API |
|---------|-----------|-----|
| **Custom Instructions** | ✅ Basic | ✅ Full system prompts |

| **Prompt Caching** | ❌ | ✅ |
| **File Management** | ✅ Simple | ✅ Programmatic |

- Use custom instructions for your thinking style
- Leverage projects to organize by topic
- This stays conversational and exploratory

- **Simple scripts:** Claude Code (faster iteration)

# Complete Guide to Extending and Customizing Claude

Let me give you the full landscape of what's available across your three use cases.

## Extension Patterns by Platform

### Claude.ai
**Best for:** Brainstorming, one-off tasks, team collaboration

| Extension | How to Use | What It Does | Persistence |
|-----------|-----------|-------------|------------|
| **Projects** | Create project → add context files/links | Persistent context across conversations | Per-project (reusable across sessions) |
| **Skills** | Settings > Capabilities > Skills → upload ZIP | Reusable workflows auto-triggered by keywords | Across all conversations |
| **MCP Connectors** | Settings > Capabilities > Connected apps | Real-time service integrations (Slack, GitHub, etc.) | Lives in Settings |

**Brainstorming workflow example:**
- Create a Project for your product concept with market research, design docs, customer feedback
- Upload a Skill with your company's naming conventions, tone guidelines, brand philosophy
- Claude remembers both across all conversations in that project

---

### Claude Code (Your Development Hub)
**Best for:** Development workflows, automation, multi-step orchestration

This is where you get the richest extension system. Everything from Claude.ai **plus**:

| Extension | How to Use | What It Does | Best For |
|-----------|-----------|-------------|----------|
| **CLAUDE.md** | Create in project root (~200 lines) | "Always follow these rules" — auto-loaded every request | Developer rules, code style, testing patterns |
| **.claude/rules/** | Subdirectory of .claude/ | Overflow rules (split complex CLAUDE.md) | Organized governance |
| **Skills** (filesystem) | Create in `.claude/skills/` folder | Named skills: `/skillname` or auto-triggered | Reusable workflows without keywords |
| **Hooks** | Define in `.claude/hooks/` (shell + HTTP) | Deterministic automation: pre/post request, file watch | CI/CD integration, auto-commits, format checks |
| **Plugins** | Bundle skills + hooks + MCP + settings (ZIP) | Distribute your setup to teammates | Team standardization |
| **MCP** | Direct connection to MCP servers (stdio/HTTP/SSE) | Full programmatic access to external systems | Database queries, real-time data, custom tools |
| **Subagents** | Use `Agent` tool in code | Isolated workers with own context + tool sets | Parallel tasks, focused domains |
| **Agent Teams** | Coordinate multiple subagents | Agents communicate and hand off work | Complex multi-domain workflows |
| **Background Tasks** | `Ctrl+B` or hook-triggered | Long-running monitors (polling, cron) | Watch builds, run tests, check deployments |
| **/loop** | `/loop <interval>` command | Repeat task every N seconds/minutes | Polling-based monitoring |

**Development workflow example:**
```
.claude/
  CLAUDE.md              # "Always run tests before commits"
  rules/
    testing.md           # Test patterns
    api-standards.md     # API guidelines
  skills/
    /test-suite.md       # Automated test runner
    /review.md           # Code review checklist
  hooks/
    post-request.sh      # Auto-format after each response
    ci-watch.http        # Poll CI status
```

**Powerful combinations:**
- **Hook + Skill + Subagent:** After each commit (hook) → run `/review` (skill) → spawn code review agent (subagent)
- **Background task + MCP:** Monitor database (background) → MCP query on changes → trigger subagent
- **Code Review:** Managed PR review ($15-25/review, Teams/Enterprise tier)

---

### API (Direct, Bedrock, Vertex AI, Azure)
**Best for:** Programmatic orchestration, custom products, scaling

You don't install extensions here—you *orchestrate* them via code:

| Pattern | What You Control | Use When |
|---------|-----------------|----------|
| **Messages API** | Full request/response cycle | One-off tasks, single-model queries |
| **Agent SDK** (Python/TS) | Persistent conversations, custom tools, hooks | Multi-step workflows, custom transport |
| **Batch API** | Async bulk processing (50% discount) | High-volume classification, bulk analysis |
| **Files API** | Persistent file storage (500MB/file, 100GB/org) | Share documents across requests, long-term reference |
| **Tool use** | Build custom tooling | Extend Claude's capabilities in your app |
| **Programmatic tool calling** | Execute tools without round-trips | Reduce latency in tool-heavy workflows |
| **MCP Connector** | Connect remote MCP servers | Reuse Claude Code/Desktop integrations |

**Product example (SaaS app):**
```python
from anthropic import Anthropic

client = Anthropic()

# Persistent conversation with tool use
conversation = []

while True:
    user_input = input("You: ")
    
    # Add web search + code execution for this request
    response = client.messages.create(
        model="claude-opus-4-6",
        max_tokens=4096,
        tools=[
            {"type": "web_search_20260209", "name": "web_search"},
            {"type": "code_execution_20260120", "name": "code_execution"}
        ],
        system="You are a research assistant. Use web search and code to answer accurately.",
        messages=conversation + [{"role": "user", "content": user_input}]
    )
    
    conversation.append({"role": "user", "content": user_input})
    conversation.append({"role": "assistant", "content": response.content})
    
    print(f"Claude: {response.content[0].text}")
```

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Code Execution: API vs Claude.com

There are some important differences:

## Claude.com (claude.ai)
- Has a **built-in code interpreter** for Python, JavaScript, and other languages
- Executes code in a sandboxed environment
- Results are displayed inline in the conversation
- Good for exploration and prototyping

## Anthropic API
- You get the **`computer_use` tool** (not a direct code execution tool)
- This tool lets Claude interact with a computer/environment, including running code
- But **you build and control the execution environment**
- More flexible but requires you to set it up

## Key Differences

| Aspect | Claude.com | API |
|--------|-----------|-----|
| **Setup** | Ready to use | You implement the environment |
| **Control** | Limited | Full control over capabilities |
| **Execution** | Pre-configured sandbox | You define what's allowed |
| **Data access** | Isolated | You manage data flow |

## For Your Use Case

If your developers are using Claude.com directly, they're getting ad-hoc code execution but **not integrated with your API**. For production integration:

1. **Use the API** with `computer_use` for consistent, controlled execution
2. **Document the difference** to your team so they know Claude.com exploration ≠ production behavior
3. Consider whether you need to replicate Claude.com's quick interpreter functionality for development

What's your main concern—ensuring consistency, or making sure developers understand the tooling difference?

</details>

#### Treatment Response
- Accuracy keywords matched: ['code_execution', 'api', 'claude code', 'bash']
- Completeness keywords matched: ['sandbox', 'python', 'filesystem']
- Deprecated patterns found: []
- Judge — Accuracy: 2, Completeness: 3, Actionability: 2

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

Great question—there's an important distinction here between the **API's code execution tool** and **Claude Code's built-in code execution**. They're similar in spirit but different in scope and purpose.

## API Code Execution Tool

When you call the API with `tools: [{"type": "code_execution_20260120", "name": "code_execution"}]`, Claude:
- Runs Python code in a **sandboxed container**
- Has access to common libraries (pandas, numpy, requests, etc.)
- Can read/write files within the sandbox
- Executes synchronously within the API request
- Results streamed back to your application

**Key constraint**: Designed for *single-step analysis tasks*—data transformation, calculations, parsing. The sandbox is ephemeral (doesn't persist between requests).

## Claude Code's Code Execution

Claude Code developers get **much broader** capabilities:
- Full **filesystem access** (read/write files in your project)
- **Long-running processes** (can spin up servers, watch directories)
- **Background tasks** (`Ctrl+B`) and **scheduling** (`/loop` for recurring jobs)
- **Shell access** (run arbitrary commands, git operations, npm scripts)
- **Multi-step orchestration**—code execution is just one piece of a larger workflow
- **Direct IDE integration** (VS Code, JetBrains, etc.)

It's less "sandboxed tool" and more "Claude as a development environment participant."

## Quick Comparison

| Aspect | API Code Execution | Claude Code |
|--------|---|---|
| **Environment** | Ephemeral sandbox | Your filesystem |
| **Duration** | Single request | Persistent session |
| **Shell access** | No | Yes |
| **File persistence** | No (sandbox is temp) | Yes |
| **Async/background tasks** | No | Yes (`/loop`, `Ctrl+B`) |
| **Use case** | Data analysis, transformations | Full development workflows |
| **Pricing** | Free (when used with web search/fetch) | Included in Claude Code plan |

## For Your Situation

**If your API integration needs data analysis:**
- Use the **API code execution tool**—it's built for this and free
- Works great for one-shot analytical tasks (transform input → return results)
- Scale it across requests; each is independent

**If your Claude Code developers are doing heavier work:**
- They'll naturally leverage **shell access**, **file I/O**, and **background tasks**
- You can guide them to use `/loop` for monitoring jobs or `Ctrl+B` for long-running processes
- Their workflows will be richer (e.g., run analysis → commit results → trigger CI)

**Bridge both worlds**: Your API might write results to a file or database that Claude Code developers monitor/process further—complementary, not redundant.

So to directly answer: developers using Claude Code get *far* more than the API tool provides, but that's intentional—they're operating in a different context (local IDE vs. remote API call).

</details>

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

You're describing a multi-step agent workflow with step-specific instructions — **Claude.ai cannot do this natively**. You'll need to upgrade to **Claude Code** for full support.

Here's why and what your options are:

## Why Claude.ai Falls Short

Claude.ai is designed for conversational tasks. It lacks:
- **Code execution** (needed to run tests)
- **Multi-step orchestration** (each step needs its own system prompt/tools)
- **Filesystem access** (to review local code, create PRs)
- **Deterministic automation** (repeatable workflows without user interaction)

Even with Projects (persistent context), you'd manually trigger each step and copy-paste results between conversations.

## Solution: Upgrade to Claude Code

**Claude Code** gives you everything you need:

1. **Subagents** — isolated workers with separate system prompts:
   ```
   Code Review Agent (prompt: "focus on security & readability")
   Test Runner Agent (prompt: "run tests, report coverage")
   PR Creator Agent (prompt: "write clear commit messages")
   ```

2. **Code execution** — run tests, call APIs, manage files directly

3. **Hooks** — automate triggers (e.g., "after PR creation, notify Slack")

4. **Agent teams** — orchestrate the 3 subagents in sequence

### Example Workflow in Claude Code

You'd structure it like:
```
Main Agent
  ├─ Subagent 1: Code Review
  │  └─ System prompt: "Review for security, performance, style"
  │  └─ Tools: file access, code analysis
  │
  ├─ Subagent 2: Test Runner
  │  └─ System prompt: "Run tests, report failures clearly"
  │  └─ Tools: bash, code execution
  │
  └─ Subagent 3: PR Creator
     └─ System prompt: "Write concise, semantic commit messages"
     └─ Tools: GitHub API, file I/O
```

Each step runs sequentially, with the main agent passing output from one to the next.

## Lighter Alternative: Agent SDK

If you want to stay **programmatic** (not in Claude Code's UI), use the **Agent SDK** (Python/TypeScript):

```python
from anthropic import Anthropic

client = Anthropic()

# Step 1: Code review
review = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=2048,
    system="You are a code reviewer. Focus on security and readability.",
    messages=[{"role": "user", "content": code_content}]
)

# Step 2: Run tests
test_result = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=2048,
    system="Run tests and report coverage.",
    messages=[{"role": "user", "content": f"Review complete. Now test:\n{review.content[0].text}"}]
)

# Step 3: Create PR
pr_result = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=2048,
    system="Write a clear PR with semantic commit message.",
    messages=[{"role": "user", "content": f"Tests passed. Create PR:\n{test_result.content[0].text}"}]
)
```

This is **fully automatable** but requires running code outside of Claude.ai.

## Quick Comparison

| Feature | Claude.ai | Claude Code | Agent SDK |
|---------|-----------|-------------|-----------|
| Step-specific prompts | ❌ | ✅ (subagents) | ✅ |
| Code execution | ❌ | ✅ | ✅ (via tool_use) |
| Multi-step orchestration | ❌ | ✅ (agent teams) | ✅ |
| Deterministic automation | ❌ | ✅ (hooks) | ✅ |
| UI-based | ✅ | ✅ | ❌ |
| Programmatic only | ❌ | ❌ | ✅ |

## My Recommendation

- **Best UX + features**: **Claude Code** — full orchestration, no coding required, repeatable
- **Lightweight automation**: **Agent SDK** — full control, integrates into your CI/CD
- **Quick prototyping**: Stay on Claude.ai but manually manage steps (not scalable)

If you're serious about automating this workflow, **Claude Code** is the natural fit — it's built exactly for this use case.

</details>

# Data Privacy & Contract Review: Your Questions Answered

Great question—this is a legitimate concern that many organizations have. Let me address both directly.

## Training & Data Usage

**Short answer: Your conversations are not used to train Claude.**

- Anthropic does **not** train on API conversations by default
- Anthropic does **not** train on Claude.ai conversations by default
- Your data is not retained for model improvement
- Anthropic has a [public privacy policy](https://www.anthropic.com/privacy) and [terms of service](https://www.anthropic.com/legal/consumer-terms) you can review

This is a fundamental difference from some other AI services. It's one of Anthropic's stated commitments.

## Using Claude for Confidential Documents

**It's generally safe, but with caveats:**

### ✅ What's Safe
- Pasting contract text into Claude (via API or Claude.ai)
- Uploading PDFs of contracts
- Asking Claude to identify risks, explain terms, or flag unusual clauses
- Using Claude's analysis within your organization

### ⚠️ Best Practices to Follow

1. **Redact sensitive info** where feasible
   - Remove specific dollar amounts, personal names, exact dates if they're not central to the question
   - Keep commercial terms and legal language intact (that's what Claude analyzes anyway)

2. **Use the API if you need audit trails**
   - If your organization requires logging/compliance records, use the Claude API
   - You control the infrastructure and can implement additional security measures
   - Claude.ai conversations have an audit trail (viewable in your account settings)

3. **Consider your organization's data policies**
   - Some enterprises have blanket policies against sending external data to third parties
   - Check with your legal/compliance team first—it's not about Claude's safety, but your org's rules

4. **Don't rely on Claude as your only reviewer**
   - Use Claude to **accelerate** your review (spot-check risks, explain dense clauses)
   - Always have a lawyer review critical contracts for legal advice
   - Claude is excellent at structural analysis but may miss jurisdiction-specific risks

### 🔒 Additional Security Options

- **Enterprise agreement with Anthropic**: If you have sensitive volume, you can arrange SOC 2 compliance certifications, data processing agreements, or self-hosted arrangements
- **Prompt caching**: If reviewing multiple versions of the same contract, caching keeps data within Anthropic's systems without re-processing

## Practical Workflow

```
1. Redact (remove company-specific data if not essential)
2. Paste into Claude or use the Files API
3. Ask Claude to:
   - Flag unusual terms
   - Summarize obligations
   - Identify missing standard clauses
   - Explain legal jargon
4. Create a summary for your lawyer
5. Have your lawyer do final review
```

## What to Tell Your Boss

*"Claude is safe for confidential contracts because Anthropic doesn't train on conversations. I've checked our compliance requirements and can use it to accelerate analysis—spotting risks, explaining terms, and creating a checklist for legal review. But I'll have our lawyer do the final sign-off."*

---

**Bottom line**: The privacy concern is real but resolved by Anthropic's policy. The bigger question is whether your organization's own data governance rules allow it. A quick chat with your legal/compliance team takes 5 minutes and gives you confidence.

</details>

Claude can handle both tasks, but with some important caveats:

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Yes—there are several ways to do this depending on where you use Claude:

## **Best Option: Projects (Claude.ai & Desktop)**
If you're on **Claude.ai or Claude Desktop**, use **Projects**:
- Create a project for your company
- Add your company info, writing style guide, and any reference docs to the project context
- Start a new chat *within* that project—Claude will automatically load all that context
- Every chat in the project has access to the same persistent information

This is the simplest approach and requires no setup beyond organizing your docs.

## **For Claude Code (CLI/IDE)**
If you use **Claude Code** (VS Code, JetBrains, CLI), you have more options:

1. **CLAUDE.md** (simplest)
   - Create a `CLAUDE.md` file in your project root with your company overview, style guide, and key facts (~200 lines max)
   - Claude loads this automatically in every conversation
   - Works great for consistent context across all chats

2. **Skills** (for repeatable workflows)
   - Create a skill that encodes your writing style, company voice, or specific processes
   - Auto-invokes when relevant
   - Better than CLAUDE.md if you have complex, multi-step guidelines

3. **`.claude/rules/`** (for overflow)
   - If your CLAUDE.md gets too long, split rules into separate files in `.claude/rules/`
   - Automatically loaded alongside CLAUDE.md

## **For API/Programmatic Use**
If you're building a custom app, use the **Memory tool**:
- Stores facts about your company in persistent memory
- Claude recalls relevant facts automatically
- Requires client-side storage of memory snapshots

---

## **Quick Decision Tree**
- **Claude.ai/Desktop** → Use **Projects** ✓
- **Claude Code** → Start with **CLAUDE.md**, add **Skills** if you have complex workflows
- **Building a custom app** → Use the **Memory tool**
- **API-only (no IDE/Desktop)** → System prompt + batch uploads via Files API as a workaround

**Which platform are you primarily using?** That'll help me give you more specific setup steps.

</details>

# Claude Can Generate Both PowerPoint and Excel Files

Good news: Claude can create both **PowerPoint presentations (.pptx)** and **Excel spreadsheets (.xlsx)** directly. Here's how:

## How It Works

Claude generates these files through **code execution** using Python libraries:
- **PowerPoint**: `python-pptx` library
- **Excel**: `openpyxl` or `pandas` library

You write the content/data, Claude writes the Python code to structure it into the file format, executes it, and the file is ready to download.

## Which Platform Matters

**Files can be generated on:**
- **Claude Code** (CLI, VS Code, JetBrains, Desktop app) — full support
- **Claude.ai/web** — supported via **Agent Skills** (document generation feature)
- **Desktop app** — supported via skills
- **API** — via code execution tool

**Cannot generate directly on:**
- CoWork (browser automation only)

## What You Can Build

For your use case, Claude can easily create:

### PowerPoint Presentations
- Slide layouts (title, bullet points, images)
- Text formatting (fonts, colors, sizes)
- Multiple slide types
- Tables and shapes
- Speaker notes

### Excel Spreadsheets
- Multiple sheets
- Formulas (SUM, IF, VLOOKUP, etc.)
- Formatting (borders, fills, fonts, number formats)
- Charts and graphs
- Conditional formatting
- Currency/accounting formats for costings

## Quick Example Flow

```
You: "Create a PowerPoint with 5 slides about our Q4 roadmap"
→ Claude writes Python code using python-pptx
→ Code executes and generates presentation.pptx
→ You download the file
```

## Practical Tips for Your Project

**For the pitch deck:**
- Describe the slide content and flow
- Claude will handle layout/formatting
- Mention your brand colors/fonts if you have preferences
- You can request specific slide types (agenda, data, testimonials, etc.)

**For cost projections:**
- Provide the line items and rates
- Specify any formulas (markup %, contingency calculations)
- Request specific columns (cost, quantity, total, etc.)
- Claude can add currency formatting and summary rows automatically

If you're using **Claude Code**, you can start working on these files immediately. On **Claude.ai/web**, check that you have document generation enabled (available in Claude 4/Plus tier with the right settings).

# Customizing Claude for Your Company

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

Unfortunately, **Claude doesn't support fine-tuning**. But you have several excellent alternatives depending on your needs:

## Best Options by Use Case

### 1. **System Prompts + Projects (Claude.ai/Desktop)** — Best for most teams
Perfect for terminology, house style, and consistent behavior across conversations.

- Create a **Project** with your style guide, glossary, and examples
- Write a **system prompt** that covers:
  - Your terminology definitions
  - Writing style (tone, formatting, abbreviations)
  - Company-specific conventions
  - Examples of "good" output in your style

**Advantages**: Zero setup, free, persistent context, works immediately.

**Example system prompt structure**:
```
You are writing for [Company]. Always follow these rules:

TERMINOLOGY:
- "API gateway" (not "API proxy")
- "data pipeline" (not "ETL")
- Use "we" for company perspective

STYLE:
- Oxford commas required
- Headings in title case
- Code examples in Python unless specified

TONE: Professional but conversational, avoid jargon unless necessary
```

### 2. **CLAUDE.md + Skills (Claude Code)** — For development teams
For persistent, always-loaded context in Claude Code.

- **CLAUDE.md** (~200 lines max): your core rules, terminology, style
- **Skills**: reusable workflows (e.g., `/brand-check` to audit copy against guidelines)
- **.claude/rules/** subdirectory: overflow your guidelines without bloating CLAUDE.md

**Advantages**: Survives across projects, filesystem integration, can auto-invoke.

```markdown
# Company Style Guide

## Terminology
- Use "platform" not "system"
- "workspace" not "project"

## Output Rules
- Always include a TOC for docs >500 words
- Format code examples with syntax highlighting
```

### 3. **Memory Tool (API)** — For custom applications
If you're building a custom app with the Messages API.

- Persist learned preferences (terminology, style choices) across sessions
- Store company facts the user references once
- Build on it gradually

**Advantages**: Client-side control, scales across users.

### 4. **RAG + Prompt Caching (API)** — For large documents
If you have extensive documentation, legal templates, or style guides.

- Upload via **Files API** or embed in system prompt with **prompt caching**
- Claude reads and applies your rules in every request
- Cache persists (5-min or 1-hour), reducing costs

**Best for**: 50+ page style guides, product documentation, compliance rules.

---

## Practical Implementation

### **Quick Start (Claude.ai/Desktop)**
1. Open **Settings → Workspace Settings**
2. Create a **Project** called "Company Style"
3. Write a system prompt with your terminology + style rules
4. Share the Project link with teammates

### **For Claude Code Users**
Create `.claude/CLAUDE.md`:
```markdown
# [Company] Guidelines

## Terminology
[Your terms]

## Code Style
[Your conventions]

## Writing Style
[Your rules]
```

Then create a skill (`skills/brand-check.js`) to auto-audit output:
```javascript
module.exports = {
  name: "brand-check",
  description: "Verify text matches company style",
  async execute(text) {
    // Check for forbidden terms, style violations
    return violations;
  }
};
```

### **For API Integration**
Include style guide in system prompt + use prompt caching:

```python
from anthropic import Anthropic

STYLE_GUIDE = """
COMPANY TERMINOLOGY:
- "platform" not "system"
- [more terms...]

WRITING STYLE:
- Oxford commas required
- [more rules...]
"""

client = Anthropic()
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=2048,
    system=[
        {
            "type": "text",
            "text": STYLE_GUIDE,
            "cache_control": {"type": "ephemeral"}
        }
    ],
    messages=[{"role": "user", "content": "Write our marketing copy..."}]
)
```

---

## What Works Best

| Scenario | Best Solution |
|----------|---------------|
| Share style across your team | **Projects** (Claude.ai/Desktop) |
| Development-heavy workflows | **CLAUDE.md + Skills** (Claude Code) |
| Large style guides (50+ pages) | **Prompt caching** + Files API |
| Progressive learning per user | **Memory tool** (custom app) |
| One-off refinement | System prompt in the conversation |

## Key Advantage Over Fine-Tuning

You get **instant updates** — change a term in your Project or CLAUDE.md, and all future conversations use the new rule. No retraining, no wait time.

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Yes, you should be concerned. Here are the key risks:

## Data Privacy & Security Issues

**Claude.ai's free version sends your data to Anthropic's servers.** Your office admin is uploading:
- Real client names
- Project details (potentially proprietary)
- Email content (which may contain sensitive business info)

**Anthropic's policy on free tier data:**
- Free conversations may be reviewed by Anthropic staff for safety/improvement purposes
- Data is stored and could theoretically be accessed if systems are breached
- You have no data processing agreement (DPA) or enterprise safeguards

This violates best practices for:
- **Client confidentiality** — clients expect their names/details stay private
- **Compliance** — if you handle regulated data (healthcare, finance, GDPR-subject data), this is likely illegal
- **Contract obligations** — many client contracts require you to protect their information

## What to Do

**Immediate steps:**
1. **Stop using free Claude** for any real client data
2. **Switch to Claude.ai with a paid plan** or **Claude API** with enterprise controls
3. **Review what's been drafted** — consider if clients need to be notified
4. **Check your compliance obligations** — GDPR, HIPAA, industry standards, client contracts

**Better options:**
- **Claude.ai Pro/Teams** ($20/mo or team pricing) — still cloud-based, but you get terms of service that are more business-friendly
- **Claude API** (direct) — with your own infrastructure, you control data handling completely
- **Claude Code** (enterprise) — full control with your own deployment options

**For your admin:**
- Create a clear policy: "No real client names, project details, or identifiable info in free tools"
- If budget allows, get them Claude.ai Pro or set up API access with proper data handling

## The Real Risk

The **biggest risk isn't Anthropic being malicious** — it's that:
- Your clients find out their data went to a third party
- You lose client trust and face legal consequences
- You violate compliance requirements (which can be expensive)

Even if the likelihood of a breach is low, the *exposure* is high. Better to be safe and use tools designed for business use.

</details>

# Yes, Claude can automate this—and you have several options depending on how you want to set things up.

## What Claude Can Do

Claude can:
- **Extract data from invoices** (vision capabilities handle PDFs, images, scanned docs)
- **Format data into spreadsheets** (generate Excel/CSV or update via API)
- **Compose summary emails** with structured data
- **Schedule this weekly** so it runs every Monday without manual intervention

## Your Options (Ranked by Ease)

### 1. **Claude Code (Recommended for Automation)**
**Best if:** You want true automation that runs on a schedule without your input.

Set up in **Claude Code** (`claude-code` CLI or VS Code/JetBrains extension):
- Use the **`/loop` command** to schedule the task for every Monday
- Claude reads your invoices (from a folder or API), extracts data, updates the spreadsheet, and sends the email—all automatically
- **Background tasks** (`Ctrl+B`) let you set it and forget it
- Use **hooks** (deterministic shell scripts) to integrate with your email/spreadsheet tools (e.g., `curl` to Gmail API, `python-excel` for sheets)

**Setup time:** 30–45 minutes. **Cost:** Minimal (runs weekly, short task).

```
/loop every Monday at 9am
Extract invoices from ~/invoices/, update ~/data.xlsx, send summary to manager@company.com
```

---

### 2. **Agent SDK (For Custom Apps)**
**Best if:** You want to embed this in your own app or integrate with custom systems.

Use the **Agent SDK** (Python or TypeScript) with Claude:
- Write a script that runs on your server/machine
- Claude handles the data extraction and formatting logic
- You control when/where it runs (your scheduler, your server)

**Typical flow:**
```python
from anthropic import Anthropic

client = Anthropic()
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4.6",
    max_tokens=2048,
    messages=[{
        "role": "user",
        "content": "Extract invoice data from ~/invoices and format as CSV"
    }],
    tools=[...]  # code_execution, file access, etc.
)
```

**Setup time:** 1–2 hours. **Cost:** Pay per API call.

---

### 3. **Claude.ai + Projects (Manual Trigger, Persistent Context)**
**Best if:** You want simplicity and don't mind triggering it yourself each Monday.

- Create a **Project** in Claude.ai with your invoice templates and instructions
- Upload invoices each Monday, Claude extracts data in seconds
- Copy-paste the output into your spreadsheet manually (5 min)
- Use Claude to draft the summary email

**Limitations:** Not automated—you still start the process. But very low friction.

**Setup time:** 10 minutes. **Cost:** Free (or Claude Pro subscription).

---

### 4. **Build a Skill (For Reuse)**
**Best if:** You want to package this workflow to share or reuse across projects.

Create a **skill** (ZIP file with instructions + example data) that Claude automatically invokes when you mention extracting invoices. Available on Claude.ai, Desktop, and Claude Code.

**Setup time:** 20 minutes. **Cost:** Free.

---

## My Recommendation

**Start with Claude Code + `/loop`** if:
- You want full automation (runs every Monday, no manual steps)
- Your invoices are in a consistent format
- You have access to APIs for your spreadsheet (Google Sheets, Excel Online) and email

**Fall back to Agent SDK** if Claude Code doesn't integrate with your specific tools.

**Use Claude.ai/Projects** if you want zero setup friction and don't mind 5 minutes of manual work weekly.

Great question! Claude Pro gives you access to some powerful capabilities beyond basic chat. Here's what can actually save you time:

## High-Impact Use Cases

**Document & Code Analysis**
- Upload PDFs, Word docs, spreadsheets, or code files — Claude reads them in seconds
- Extract key info, summarize long documents, spot bugs, refactor code
- Analyze multiple files in one go to find patterns or inconsistencies

**Content & Writing**
- Draft emails, reports, proposals — then iterate until they match your tone
- Rewrite for different audiences (technical → executive summary)

- Upload screenshots, diagrams, charts — Claude describes them or extracts data
- Useful for documenting bugs, analyzing designs, processing forms

**Structured Output**
- Ask Claude to extract data into tables or organized lists (not just prose)

### Test 9.12: Conversational Platform Users

**Prompt:** I want to build a search system over our 500 company documents so staff can ask questions and get answers. Can Claude create embeddings for our documents, or do I need something else for that part?

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Claude and Document Search

Claude itself **cannot create embeddings** — that's not part of its capabilities. However, you have good options:

## What you actually need:

1. **An embedding model** (separate from Claude) to convert documents into vectors
2. **A vector database** to store and search those embeddings
3. **Claude** to answer questions based on retrieved documents

## Practical solutions:

**Easiest approach:**
- Use **Voyage AI** or **OpenAI's embedding API** for embeddings
- Store in **Pinecone** or **Weaviate** (managed vector DBs — minimal setup)
- Query the DB, then send results to Claude for answer generation

**More control:**
- Use open-source embeddings like **sentence-transformers** (run locally)
- Store in **PostgreSQL + pgvector** or **Milvus** (self-hosted)

**Fully managed:**
- Anthropic's **Files API** (if <20MB per document) lets you upload PDFs directly to Claude without separate embeddings, though it's slower for 500 documents

## My recommendation for your case:

For 500 documents, I'd suggest:
- **Embed with:** Voyage AI or OpenAI API
- **Store in:** Pinecone (free tier might work, simple setup)
- **Answer with:** Claude's API

This keeps things simple while scaling well.

Want help with the implementation architecture?

</details>

#### Treatment Response
- Accuracy keywords matched: ['no embedding', 'voyage', 'rag', '1m']
- Completeness keywords matched: ['search']
- Deprecated patterns found: []
- Judge — Accuracy: 2, Completeness: 2, Actionability: 2

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

Claude doesn't offer embeddings, so you'll need a separate embeddings model for that part of the pipeline. Here's what you need to build:

## Architecture Overview

**Three components:**
1. **Embeddings model** (separate) → vectorize your 500 documents
2. **Vector database** → store and search those vectors
3. **Claude** → answer questions using retrieved documents

## Recommended Embeddings + Vector DB Stack

**Popular combinations:**
- **Voyage AI embeddings** + Pinecone/Weaviate/Milvus (managed vector DBs)
- **OpenAI text-embedding-3-small** + Postgres with pgvector
- **Cohere embeddings** + Qdrant
- **Open-source** (Hugging Face models) + self-hosted vector DB

Voyage is a solid choice—built for retrieval tasks, works well with Claude, has a generous free tier.

## High-Level Flow

```
1. Chunk & embed your 500 docs → vector DB
2. User asks a question
3. Embed the question (same model)
4. Search vector DB for top-K similar documents
5. Pass retrieved docs + question to Claude
6. Claude synthesizes the answer
```

## Integration with Claude

Once you have retrieval working, pass the results to Claude via **two patterns**:

**Pattern A: Simple RAG** (most common)
- Retrieve top 5-10 documents
- Put them in the user message
- Claude reads and answers

```python
# Pseudocode
question = "What's our vacation policy?"
docs = vector_db.search(embed(question), top_k=5)
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=1024,
    messages=[{
        "role": "user",
        "content": f"Documents:\n\n{docs}\n\nQuestion: {question}"
    }]
)
```

**Pattern B: Web Search + RAG** (if you want Claude to augment with external info)
- Retrieve from your docs
- Let Claude also use web search
- Combine both sources

```python
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=1024,
    tools=[{"type": "web_search_20250305", "name": "web_search"}],
    messages=[{
        "role": "user",
        "content": f"Internal docs:\n\n{docs}\n\nQuestion: {question}"
    }]
)
```

## Practical Considerations

**Document size:** With 500 docs, you'll likely fit them all in Claude's context (up to 200K on standard, 1M on beta with header). If docs are huge, chunk them before embedding.

**Update frequency:** If documents change often, you'll need to re-embed and update the vector DB. Plan for a refresh pipeline.

**Cost:** Embeddings are cheap (~$0.02 per million tokens). Vector DB can be free (self-hosted) or ~$10-50/month (managed).

## Next Steps

1. **Pick an embeddings provider** (Voyage, OpenAI, Cohere)
2. **Pick a vector DB** (Pinecone, Weaviate, or Postgres + pgvector)
3. **Chunk your 500 docs** (250-1000 token chunks work well)
4. **Embed and index** them
5. **Build the search → Claude pipeline** using the patterns above

If you're building a quick prototype, **Pinecone + Voyage** is the fastest path (both have free tiers). For production with cost control, **Postgres + pgvector + open-source embeddings** is solid.

Would you like help with any of those steps, or do you have questions about choosing between embedding providers?

</details>
