# Claude Code Review

Yes! Claude can automatically review your pull requests. Here's what you need to know:

## Availability & Setup

**Code Review** is available in **Claude Code** (Teams/Enterprise tier) and integrates with GitHub, GitLab, and Bitbucket. It's a managed service—Claude handles the review without you needing to orchestrate it.

## What It Checks

Code Review performs comprehensive analysis:

- **Logic & correctness** — identifies potential bugs, logic errors, edge cases
- **Security** — detects vulnerabilities, unsafe patterns, credential leaks
- **Performance** — flags inefficient algorithms, N+1 queries, memory issues
- **Style & best practices** — consistency with language conventions, code patterns
- **Testing** — suggests test coverage gaps, edge cases that need tests
- **Documentation** — checks clarity of comments, docstrings, API documentation
- **Maintainability** — identifies overly complex code, refactoring opportunities

The review is contextual—Claude reads the full PR diff, commit messages, and relevant file context to provide meaningful feedback.

## Pricing

Code Review costs **$15–$25 per review** (exact price depends on your Enterprise plan). The service is metered based on the size and complexity of the PR being reviewed.

## How to Use It

In Claude Code, after pushing a branch and opening a PR:

1. **Link your repo** — authenticate with GitHub/GitLab/Bitbucket via Claude Code settings
2. **Trigger reviews** — either:
   - Manually request a review on the PR
   - Set up automation so Claude reviews all PRs in certain repos
3. **View feedback** — Claude posts comments on the PR highlighting issues, with explanations and suggested fixes

The review appears as a standard PR comment, so your team can discuss and approve changes in your normal workflow.

## Requirements

- **Claude Code** with Teams/Enterprise tier
- **Repository access** — your repo must be connected to Claude Code
- **PR context** — works best with clear commit messages and file structure

---

**Not sure if Code Review is right for you?** It's ideal for teams that want continuous, cost-effective review automation without hiring additional reviewers. For simpler use cases, you might combine Claude Code's general coding assistance with manual team reviews.

# Claude Code Session Continuity

Unfortunately, **you cannot directly continue a Claude Code session across devices**. Here's why and what you can do instead:

## The Challenge
- Claude Code sessions are tied to your current browser/device
- Sessions don't persist or sync across different devices
- Starting a new chat on your phone would begin a fresh session

## Your Options

1. **Save your work before leaving**
   - Copy/export any code you've written
   - Take screenshots or notes of your progress
   - Save files to cloud storage (GitHub, Google Drive, etc.)

2. **Resume on phone with context**
   - Share your code in the new chat on your phone
   - Paste the relevant code and ask Claude to continue from where you left off
   - This works well, just requires providing the context again

3. **Use cloud-based alternatives**
   - If your code is on GitHub, you could work there directly
   - Cloud IDEs like Replit, Codepen, or VS Code Web might be more phone-friendly

4. **Plan ahead next time**
   - Consider saving work to a persistent location before switching devices

The copy-and-paste approach is often fastest—Claude can pick up right where you left off if you provide the relevant context.

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

Yes! Claude Code has **Remote Control** built in, which is perfect for this scenario.

## How to use it:

**On your laptop (before you leave):**
1. Run `claude remote-control` in your terminal
2. This starts a remote session and gives you a shareable link

**On your phone (on the bus):**
1. Open that link in your browser
2. You can view your current session and steer Claude's work in real-time
3. Send new messages, review code, approve tool calls — all from your phone's browser

## Key capabilities while remote:

- **View the session state** — see what Claude is currently working on
- **Send messages** — guide Claude in new directions
- **Approve/reject tool calls** — maintain control while Claude executes
- **Monitor progress** — watch code execution, tests, file changes happen live

## When you're back at your laptop:

Simply close the remote session, and you can **pull back** the full context with `/teleport` if needed, or just continue your local Claude Code session where you left off.

**Note:** This works best if you have a stable internet connection. If you need to continue truly offline, your local session on the laptop will persist — you just won't be able to steer it remotely until you're back with an internet connection.

This is one of the big advantages of Claude Code over Claude.ai — it's designed for distributed, persistent work across devices.

# Running Claude Code Tasks in the Cloud

You're looking for Claude Code's **remote execution** capability. Here's how to set it up:

## Quick Setup

1. **Start a remote session from your terminal:**
   ```bash
   claude remote-control
   ```
   This launches a cloud-hosted Claude Code session and gives you a web URL.

2. **Access it from anywhere:**
   Open the URL in your browser on any device. Your Claude Code session runs in the cloud.

3. **Close your laptop:**
   The session stays alive in the cloud. You can disconnect and reconnect anytime without losing context.

## How It Works

- **`claude remote-control`** — Starts a cloud-hosted Claude Code environment
- **Web interface** — Control it via browser (no local Claude Code needed)
- **Persistent** — Session persists; you can close the browser/laptop and come back
- **Full capabilities** — Access to all Claude Code tools: skills, hooks, MCP, code execution, subagents, etc.

## Common Workflows

**Start a long-running task before closing your laptop:**
```bash
claude remote-control
# Browser opens → start your task (e.g., code review, batch processing)
# Close laptop when done
# Come back later to check results
```

**Pull results back to local:**
Use `/teleport` (in the cloud session) to transfer state back to your local Claude Code instance if needed.

## Alternative: Background Tasks

If you want fire-and-forget tasks without needing a persistent browser session:
- Use **`/loop`** for scheduled recurring tasks (runs in background)
- Or use the **Agent SDK** (Python/TypeScript) for programmatic orchestration with persistent sessions

## Requirements

- **Claude Code** installed locally (used to initiate the command)
- **Active Claude subscription** (cloud execution uses your quota)
- **Internet connection** (obviously, for the cloud part)

# Streamlining Slack to Code Fix Workflow

Yes, there are several approaches depending on your setup:

The cleanest approach: create a structured workflow that doesn't lose context:

- **Slack apps** (Jira, Linear, GitHub Issues) let you create tickets directly from messages
  - Right-click a message → "Create issue"
  - Bot commands like `/jira create` or `/linear create`
  - Automatically links discussion to ticket

- Monitors Slack for specific keywords (e.g., "bug:", #bug-reports channel)

- Posts back the ticket link so devs can grab it immediately

- Use Slack's saved messages or pins to highlight actionable bugs
- Weekly sync: review Slack bugs → prioritize into sprint

## Best Practice
The sweet spot is usually: **Slack discussion → Quick issue creation → Dev picks up issue with full context**

Yes! **Claude Code's Slack integration** is exactly what you need. Here's how it works:

## The Flow

1. **In Slack**: Team discusses a bug in any channel
2. **@Claude in thread**: Mention `@Claude` with context about the bug
3. **Automatic web session opens**: Claude Code starts a remote session in your browser
4. **Claude analyzes & fixes**: Clones the repo, reads the code, makes the fix
5. **Creates PR**: Submits the PR back to your repo—no context-switching required

## How to Set It Up

### 1. Install the Slack Integration
In Claude Code (CLI or IDE extension):
```
claude slack-setup
```
This authenticates Claude Code with your Slack workspace.

### 2. Use It in Slack
In any Slack channel or thread, mention:
```
@Claude [description of the bug or task]
```

Claude will:
- Start a **web session** (remote browser automation)
- Clone your repo
- Search the codebase
- Make the fix
- Open a PR (if you've granted repo permissions)

### 3. Steer from Slack (Optional)
You can:
- Follow the session link to **watch/steer** the fix in real-time
- Reply in the thread to give Claude new instructions mid-fix
- Approve the PR directly from Slack

## What This Solves

| Before | After |
|--------|-------|
| Copy context from Slack → Open IDE → Clone repo | @Claude in Slack → Fix + PR ready |
| Multiple people reading the same message | One person mentions @Claude once |
| Waiting for someone free to investigate | Starts immediately |
| Manual PR creation | Auto-generates PR |

## Prerequisites

- **Claude Code** (CLI: `npm install -g claude-code`, or IDE extension)
- Slack workspace admin access to install the bot
- GitHub/GitLab repo access for PR creation
- Claude subscription (Tier 2+, but Tier 3 recommended for complex fixes)

## Pro Tips

- **For complex bugs**: Reply with `/rc` (remote control) in the thread to take over the browser mid-session
- **Background tasks**: Use `/loop` to schedule recurring checks on flaky tests
- **Code review**: Use the built-in `/code-review` slash command in Claude Code to review PRs before merging
- **Team coordination**: For multi-step fixes, use **agent teams** in Claude Code to parallelize work

## Limitations

- Requires Claude Code (not Claude.ai or Desktop)
- Code execution sandbox has security boundaries (for safety)
- Very large repos may need manual repo cloning first
- PR creation needs appropriate repo permissions

This is much faster than the usual "read Slack → context-switch → fire up IDE" cycle. The whole flow typically takes 2–10 minutes depending on bug complexity.

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Remote Control vs Claude Code on the Web

These are actually **different features** with different purposes:

## Claude Code (Web)
- **What it is**: Claude's native code editor built into Claude.ai
- **Access**: Direct coding interface within the chat
- **Best for**: Writing, editing, and discussing code within conversations
- **Interaction**: You write code directly in Claude, get explanations, iterate together

## Remote Control
- **What it is**: A tool that lets Claude control your actual computer/browser
- **Access**: Claude can see your screen and interact with your mouse/keyboard
- **Best for**: 
  - Testing code in real applications
  - Automating tasks on your computer
  - Debugging issues in live environments
  - Visual verification of how something works
- **Interaction**: Claude takes actions on your system, sees results in real-time

## Simple analogy
- **Claude Code on web** = Claude helping you *write* code
- **Remote Control** = Claude *running* code and *doing things* on your actual system

## Security note
Remote Control requires explicit permission and shows you what Claude is doing. It's more powerful but requires you to opt in and maintain visibility.

**Choose Claude Code on web** for coding help and editing. **Use Remote Control** when you need Claude to actually interact with your computer or test things live.

</details>

#### Treatment Response

- Completeness keywords matched: ['/teleport', '--remote', 'mcp', 'setup script']

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

Great question—they're related but serve different purposes:

## **Remote Control** (`claude remote-control` or `/rc`)
- **Purpose**: Continue an existing Claude Code session from a different device/browser
- **How it works**: You start a session on your primary machine (laptop, VS Code, etc.), then use Remote Control to view and steer that session from anywhere else (phone, another browser, tablet)
- **Use case**: You're working in Claude Code locally, step away, and want to check progress or make quick edits from your phone
- **One-way sync**: Changes flow from the remote viewer *back* to the original session

## **Web sessions** (`--remote` flag or `/teleport`)
- **Purpose**: Run Claude Code *natively* in a browser as your primary interface
- **How it works**: Start Claude Code with `--remote` to open a browser tab that IS your Claude Code environment (not just viewing it)
- **Use case**: You want the full Claude Code experience without installing locally—code review, subagents, hooks, background tasks, MCP, everything
- **Full feature parity**: All Claude Code capabilities work (unlike viewing a local session)

## **Key Difference**
| Aspect | Remote Control | Web Sessions |
|--------|---|---|
| **Primary device** | Local (CLI/IDE) | Browser |
| **Secondary access** | View from anywhere | N/A—browser *is* primary |
| **Full Claude Code features** | Yes (on primary) | Yes (in browser) |
| **Use case** | Monitor/steer existing work | Full dev environment in browser |

**TL;DR**: Use **Remote Control** if you're already in Claude Code locally and want to peek/edit elsewhere. Use **Web sessions** (`--remote`) if you want Claude Code to *live* in your browser instead.

</details>

# Feature Parity Across Claude Access Points

The good news: **core Claude capabilities are consistent**, but there are real differences in the *experience and tooling*.

## What's the Same
- Same Claude model (Claude 3.5 Sonnet, etc.)
- Same reasoning capabilities
- Same context window limits

## Where They Differ

**Claude Code (VS Code)**
- Direct file editing and creation
- Integrated terminal access
- VSCode's debugging tools
- Inline code previews

**JetBrains (via Claude plugin)**
- Refactoring within JetBrains' ecosystem
- IDE-specific inspections and intentions
- Different UI/UX than VSCode
- Potentially different latency depending on plugin implementation

**Terminal (Claude.ai or API)**
- Most flexibility—you control everything
- No IDE integration
- Raw access to latest features first
- Manual file management

## Practical Implications
- **Feature adoption**: Terminal users often see new Claude features first
- **Productivity**: IDE integrations (both VS Code and JetBrains) typically faster for coding workflows
- **Consistency**: Core model responses should be identical, but context handling varies

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Feature Parity Across Claude Code Platforms

Good news: **Core Claude Code features are consistent across VS Code, JetBrains, and terminal (CLI)**. But there are some platform-specific differences worth knowing:

## What's Consistent Everywhere

- **Skills** (including bundled: `/simplify`, `/batch`, `/debug`, `/loop`, `/claude-api`)
- **Hooks** (shell + HTTP lifecycle automation)
- **Subagents** (`Agent` tool for isolated workers)
- **Agent teams** (parallel coordination)
- **MCP** (Model Context Protocol connections)
- **CLAUDE.md + .claude/rules/** (persistent context)
- **Code Review** (managed PR review, Teams/Enterprise, $15–25/review)
- **Background tasks** (`Ctrl+B` / `/loop` scheduling, cron tools)
- **Remote Control** (`claude remote-control` or `/rc`)
- **Web sessions** (`--remote` to start, `/teleport` to pull back)
- **All Claude models** (Opus 4.6, Sonnet 4.6, Haiku 4.5)

## Platform-Specific Differences

| Feature | VS Code | JetBrains | CLI/Terminal |
|---------|---------|-----------|--------------|
| **UI for skills/hooks** | Settings GUI | Settings GUI | Manual YAML/JSON |
| **Inline code diagnostics** | Native | Native | N/A (file-based) |
| **Background task UI** | Sidebar panel | IDE panel | Running process |
| **Remote Control viewing** | Browser + IDE | Browser + IDE | Browser only |
| **/loop scheduling UI** | Visual editor | Visual editor | CLI flags |
| **Slack integration** | Inherited | Inherited | CLI setup |

**Terminal (CLI)** is the most manual — you configure everything via YAML/JSON in `.claude/` and run commands, but you get *all* the same capabilities. No GUI shortcuts, but no limitations.

## Practical Impact

**Your team can collaborate seamlessly:**
- Skills created in VS Code work in JetBrains and CLI
- Hooks and agent configurations in `.claude/rules/` are platform-agnostic
- CLAUDE.md is the same file everywhere
- Code Review results are shared (if on Teams/Enterprise)

**Each person optimizes their workflow:**
- VS Code/JetBrains users get GUI conveniences
- CLI user gets portability and scriptability (useful for CI/CD or headless environments)

## One Thing to Check

If your **CLI user is on an older version**, update:
```bash
npm install -g @anthropic-ai/claude-code-cli
```

The three platforms should report the same or very similar version numbers (v2.1.70+).

**Bottom line:** You're all working with the same feature set. Platform choice is comfort + workflow, not capability.

# Claude vs Copilot: A Practical Comparison

## Where Claude has genuine advantages

**Context window & reasoning**
- Claude handles 200K tokens (vs Copilot's ~4K). For large codebases or complex refactoring, this matters—you can paste entire files or architectural docs for consistent suggestions
- Better at explaining *why* code does something, which helps with learning and code review

**Extended reasoning tasks**
- System design discussions, architecture decisions, migration planning
- Debugging logic-heavy problems (not just syntax)
- Writing tests and documentation alongside code

**Fewer hallucinations**
- Less likely to confidently suggest non-existent APIs (varies by model, but empirically better)

**Flexibility in workflow**
- Works in any text editor via Claude.ai or API
- No IDE lock-in; easier to use across different tools

## What you'd likely miss from Copilot

**Latency & integration**
- Copilot's in-IDE completion is near-instant and trained specifically for autocomplete. Claude's API calls add noticeable delay for line-level suggestions
- Copilot's UX is polished for the "type and it fills in" experience

**Real-time code context**
- Copilot sees your current file and nearby code automatically. With Claude, you're managing context manually (though 200K tokens reduces this friction)

**Trained on newer patterns**
- Copilot's training on GitHub gives it sharper instincts for modern idioms and popular libraries

## The honest middle ground

Most teams don't replace one with the other—they use both:
- **Copilot** for in-IDE autocomplete (speed)
- **Claude** for bigger questions: code review, architecture, complex refactors, documentation

**What to actually evaluate:** Set up Claude API or the web interface for a few days on representative tasks. The decision often hinges on whether your team values context depth and reasoning over autocomplete speed.

What's your CTO's main concern—cost, code privacy, reasoning quality, or something else?

# Claude vs GitHub Copilot: A Technical Comparison

I'll give you a direct assessment based on your likely use cases.

## What Claude Does Better

### 1. **Reasoning & Complex Problem-Solving**
- Claude's adaptive thinking (Opus 4.6/Sonnet 4.6) can tackle architectural decisions, design patterns, and multi-step refactoring that Copilot struggles with
- Better at explaining *why* a solution works, not just generating code
- **Your gain**: Fewer code reviews for logic errors; better learning for junior developers

### 2. **Context Window & Code Review**
- Claude handles 200K tokens natively (1M available on Opus 4.6 with beta header)
- Can review an entire PR, understand interdependencies, and flag issues Copilot would miss
- Built-in code review in Claude Code (managed, $15–25/PR for teams)
- **Your gain**: Catch bugs earlier; fewer post-merge issues

### 3. **Multi-Language & Framework Knowledge**
- Copilot is optimized for Python/JavaScript; Claude is stronger across Ruby, Go, Rust, uncommon frameworks
- Better at domain-specific code (finance, ML ops, embedded systems)
- **Your gain**: Better completions for your less-common tech stack

### 4. **Structured Outputs & Type Safety**
- Claude guarantees JSON schemas (`output_config.format`), making it easier to pipe code generation into linters or test generators
- Copilot can't reliably generate typed code on demand
- **Your gain**: Safer generated code; easier CI/CD integration

### 5. **Extended Reasoning (Extended & Adaptive Thinking)**
- Haiku 4.5 supports extended thinking; Opus/Sonnet 4.6 support adaptive thinking
- Can spend more compute on hard problems without token bloat
- Copilot has no equivalent
- **Your gain**: Better solutions for algorithmic code; fewer "quick hack" suggestions

### 6. **IDE Integration (Claude Code)**
- VS Code, JetBrains, Desktop app with hooks, subagents, background tasks
- Can automate code review, run tests, and commit—all in the IDE without manual intervention
- `/loop` for scheduled tasks; hooks for deterministic "after every save" actions
- **Your gain**: True workflow automation, not just completions

### 7. **MCP & Custom Tool Integration**
- Claude can connect to your internal APIs, databases, and services via MCP
- Copilot is limited to GitHub-native integrations
- **Your gain**: Contextual suggestions based on your actual codebase state, deployment status, etc.

### 8. **Batch API & Cost at Scale**
- 50% discount for async code generation (overnight linting, test generation)
- Prompt caching for shared system prompts (10% read cost after 1K tokens)
- Copilot's pricing is per-seat, not consumption-based
- **Your gain**: Better economics for large teams or high-volume generation tasks

---

## What You'd Lose

### 1. **Real-Time Completions in the Editor**
- Copilot is optimized for low-latency inline suggestions (50–200ms)
- Claude's fastest inference (Haiku) is still ~500ms–1s for streaming completions
- **Your loss**: Not ideal for rapid typing (ghost text doesn't keep up)
- **Mitigation**: Use Claude for refactoring, PR review, or multi-line suggestions; keep Copilot for inline completions if your team needs both

### 2. **Lightweight Setup**
- Copilot: Install an extension, sign in, done
- Claude Code: Requires CLI setup, environment config, or IDE plugin
- **Your loss**: Longer onboarding; more infrastructure to maintain
- **Mitigation**: Claude.ai/Desktop is instant; but programmatic integration (via API) needs setup

### 3. **Native GitHub Integration**
- Copilot Workspace, Copilot in PRs, Copilot CLI are tightly integrated
- Claude doesn't have a native GitHub app (yet)
- **Your loss**: No "suggest fixes" button in GitHub UI
- **Mitigation**: Use Claude Code or API to build your own integrations; or use Claude.ai for ad-hoc review

### 4. **Training Data Freshness**
- Copilot trained on real-time GitHub data (newer libraries, frameworks)
- Claude's training data has a cutoff (April 2024 for Sonnet 4.6; some knowledge gaps on very new frameworks)
- **Your loss**: Less awareness of bleeding-edge packages
- **Mitigation**: Use web search tool (`web_search`) in Claude to fetch latest docs on demand

### 5. **Per-Seat Predictability**
- Copilot: $10/month/seat (simple forecast)
- Claude: Pay per token (variable; depends on usage patterns)
- **Your loss**: Harder to budget; risk of overspend if not managed
- **Mitigation**: Set usage quotas; use batch API for predictable, off-peak work

### 6. **Installed-Base Network Effects**
- Copilot has plugins, integrations, and community tooling (VSCode, GitHub, countless IDEs)
- Claude ecosystem is growing but smaller
- **Your loss**: Fewer third-party integrations
- **Mitigation**: Claude Code + MCP can fill most gaps; build custom integrations if needed

---

## Replacement Scenarios

### ✅ **Claude is the Better Fit If...**
- Your team needs **code review & architectural feedback** (not just completions)
- You work in **less common languages** (Go, Rust, Elixir, etc.)
- You need **deterministic automation** (hooks, scheduled tasks, test generation)
- You have a **large codebase** and want to leverage 1M context for refactoring
- You want to **integrate with internal tools** (APIs, databases, monitoring)
- You're doing **batch processing** (overnight test generation, linting, doc generation)

### ✅ **Keep Copilot If...**
- You need **sub-second inline completions** (ghost text while typing)
- Your team is **GitHub-native** and loves the integrated workflow
- You have **predictable, per-seat budgeting** needs
- Your stack is **Python-heavy** (Copilot's sweet spot)

### 🔄 **Hybrid (Best of Both)**
- Use **Copilot** for inline completions (the real-time, low-latency job)
- Use **Claude** (Code or API) for code review, refactoring, test generation, and architectural decisions
- Cost trade-off: ~$20/seat/month (Copilot) + variable Claude API spend (often cheaper than Copilot Pro)
- **This is what many enterprises do**

---

## Evaluation Checklist for Your CTO

```
Priority: Implementation Cost vs. Benefit

❑ Run a pilot: Pick 2–3 developers, give them Claude Code for 2 weeks
❑ Measure: Completion latency, code quality (review churn), time to PR
❑ Calculate: API spend vs. Copilot seat savings
❑ Test integration: Can you plug Claude into your CI/CD, code review process, or Slack?
❑ Check your stack: Is Claude trained on your primary languages/frameworks?
❑ Plan migration: Inline completions (keep Copilot?) vs. refactor workflows (use Claude Code + hooks)
```

|---------|--------|---------|

| **Cost Model** | Per-token (batch: –50%) | $10/month/seat |
| **Custom Tools** | MCP full integration | GitHub native only |
| **Typing Speed** | Can't keep up | Designed for it |

## My Recommendation

**Don't replace—augment.** Claude excels at *leverage* (refactoring, review, architecture), while Copilot excels at *speed* (inline suggestions). A hybrid approach typically delivers the

# Claude Equivalents to ChatGPT Custom GPTs

ChatGPT's "Custom GPTs" are essentially packaged behaviors for specific tasks. Claude has several ways to achieve this depending on your needs:

## Direct Equivalents

### **Skills** (Best for Most Use Cases)
Skills are Claude's primary equivalent to custom GPTs. They're reusable knowledge/workflow packages that auto-invoke based on context.

**How they work:**
- ZIP files containing instructions, documents, and optional code
- Auto-trigger when relevant (no explicit selection needed)
- Available on **all platforms**: Claude.ai, Desktop, Claude Code, and CoWork
- Can bundle documentation, templates, datasets, and automation rules

**Example:** A "Content Calendar Manager" skill could contain templates, brand guidelines, and instructions for planning social media posts.

### **Projects** (For Persistent Context)
If your team uses Claude.ai or Desktop, **Projects** provide persistent context specific to a task or client. Think of them as "workspaces" where all conversations accumulate related context.

- Persistent across conversations
- Shared within a team (Claude.ai Teams)
- Auto-load context from previous chats

## Platform-Specific Options

| Scenario | Use | Platform |
|----------|-----|----------|
| "Always follow these rules for X task" | **Skill** | All |
| "Give this client their own context space" | **Project** | Claude.ai/Desktop |
| "Connect to external APIs/services" | **MCP** | All (varies by platform) |
| "Complex multi-step workflows" | **Subagents** | Claude Code only |
| "Deterministic automation (no tokens)" | **Hooks** | Claude Code only |
| "Recurring monitoring tasks" | **/loop** or background | Claude Code only |

## Key Differences from Custom GPTs

| Aspect | ChatGPT Custom GPTs | Claude Skills |
|--------|-------------------|---------------|
| **Knowledge files** | Upload docs, images | ZIP with files (auto-reference) |
| **Actions/APIs** | Built-in integration | MCP for service connections |
| **Instructions** | Text prompt | Text instructions + code |
| **Distribution** | Share via link | Deploy as ZIP |
| **Execution** | Chat UI only | All Claude platforms |
| **Team access** | Via Teams (paid) | Projects (Claude.ai Teams) + Skills |

## Recommended Migration Path

**If you currently use custom GPTs for:**

1. **Knowledge bases** (documents, FAQs) → **Skills** + **Projects**
   - Create a skill with your documentation
   - Use Projects to maintain client/team-specific context

2. **Task templates** (email drafts, code generation) → **Skills**
   - Package instructions and examples as a skill
   - Optional: add automation via hooks (Claude Code)

3. **API integrations** (CRM, Slack, database queries) → **MCP**
   - Set up an MCP server for your external service
   - Connect it to Claude (supported on all platforms, varies by feature set)

4. **Complex workflows** (multi-step processes) → **Skills** + **Subagents** (Claude Code)
   - Skills for individual steps
   - Subagents for orchestration with isolated context

## Practical Example: Legal Document Reviewer

**ChatGPT Custom GPT equivalent:**
- Upload company legal templates
- Add instructions for reviewing contracts
- Share with team

**Claude equivalent (Skills + Project):**
```
my-legal-skill/
├── instructions.md (review guidelines)
├── templates/ (sample contracts)
├── company-policies.pdf
└── automation/ (optional Python scripts)
```

Deploy as a skill, then:
- Create a **Project** called "Legal Reviews" 
- Invite team members to the project
- Activate the skill—it auto-triggers when reviewing documents

## Getting Started

1. **Skills**: Start by creating a ZIP with instructions + documents. See `skills.sh` registry for examples.
2. **Projects**: Available now in Claude.ai (Teams plan) and Desktop.
3. **MCP**: For API integrations, explore existing MCP servers or build one (standard protocol).

# Claude Equivalent for OpenAI Assistants API

Claude doesn't have a direct "Assistants API" equivalent, but you can build similar agent workflows using:

## 1. **Claude with Tool Use** (Closest Match)
```python
from anthropic import Anthropic

client = Anthropic()

tools = [
    {
        "name": "search_files",
        "description": "Search through uploaded documents",
        "input_schema": {
            "type": "object",
            "properties": {
                "query": {"type": "string"}
            }
        }
    },
    {
        "name": "execute_code",
        "description": "Execute Python code",
        "input_schema": {
            "type": "object",
            "properties": {
                "code": {"type": "string"}
            }
        }
    }
]

messages = []
while True:
    response = client.messages.create(
        model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
        max_tokens=4096,
        tools=tools,
        messages=messages
    )
    
    # Handle tool use in agentic loop
    if response.stop_reason == "tool_use":
        # Process tool calls
        pass
```

## 2. **Key Differences from OpenAI Assistants**

| Feature | OpenAI Assistants | Claude Approach |
|---------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **File Search** | Built-in, persistent | Implement with tool_use + custom search |
| **Code Interpreter** | Built-in sandbox | tool_use calling your code execution |
| **Persistent State** | Automatic thread management | Manual message history management |
| **Files** | Upload to API | Pass as base64 or via tool parameters |

## 3. **Building File Search**
```python
# You'll need to implement file indexing yourself
def search_files(query: str, documents: list) -> str:
    # Use Claude to search, or implement RAG
    # Option A: Simple similarity search
    # Option B: Call Claude to find relevant sections
    pass

# Or use a vector DB
from pinecone import Pinecone  # or Weaviate, etc.
```

## 4. **Code Interpreter Alternative**
```python
import subprocess
import json

def execute_code(code: str) -> str:
    try:
        result = subprocess.run(
            ["python", "-c", code],
            capture_output=True,
            timeout=30
        )
        return result.stdout.decode()
    except Exception as e:
        return f"Error: {str(e)}"
```

## 5. **Recommended Architecture**

```python
class ClaudeAgent:
    def __init__(self):
        self.client = Anthropic()
        self.message_history = []
        self.documents = []  # Your file storage
    
    def run_agent_loop(self, user_query: str):
        self.message_history.append({
            "role": "user",
            "content": user_query
        })
        
        while True:
            response = self.client.messages.create(
                model="claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
                max_tokens=4096,
                tools=self.tools,
                messages=self.message_history
            )
            
            self.message_history.append({
                "role": "assistant",
                "content": response.content
            })
            
            if response.stop_reason == "end_turn":
                return self.extract_text(response)
            
            # Process tool calls
            tool_results = self.process_tools(response)
            self.message_history.append({
                "role": "user",
                "content": tool_results
            })
```

## 6. **Best Practices for Migration**

- **File Search**: Use vector databases (Pinecone, Weaviate) + Claude embeddings
- **Code Execution**: Run in isolated environments (E2B, modal.com, or local containers)
- **Session Management**: You manage conversation history explicitly
- **Statelessness**: Claude SDK is stateless—you control persistence

## 7. **Advantages of Claude Approach**
- More control over file handling
- Flexible code execution (your infrastructure)
- Better for privacy/data handling
- Streaming support built-in
- Works with vision (images)

**For production agent systems**, most teams pair Claude with:
- **Vector DB** for file search (Pinecone, Weaviate, Milvus)
- **Code sandboxes** (E2B, Modal) for safe execution
- **Task queues** (Celery, Bull) for orchestration

Would you like me to elaborate on any of these components?

<details><summary>Full response</summary>

# Claude Equivalents for OpenAI Assistants

You have **two main paths** depending on your architecture needs:

## 1. **Messages API + Tools** (Simpler, Direct)
Best for: Single-turn or simple multi-step workflows, moderate complexity.

This is the **direct equivalent** to Assistants API. You get:

| Feature | OpenAI Assistants | Claude Messages API |
|---------|-------------------|-------------------|
| **File handling** | File search (RAG) | Files API (persistent storage) + `document` content blocks |
| **Code execution** | Code interpreter | `code_execution_20260120` tool |
| **Multi-step workflows** | Built-in via instructions | Tool use loop (you control orchestration) |
| **Persistent context** | Assistant object | Memory tool or prompt caching |
| **Structured outputs** | JSON mode | `output_config.format` (guaranteed JSON) |

**Quick example:**
```python
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=4096,
    tools=[
        {"type": "code_execution_20260120", "name": "code_execution"},
        {"type": "web_search_20260209", "name": "web_search"},
        {"type": "files_api_20250414", "name": "files"}  # upload/retrieve files
    ],
    messages=[
        {"role": "user", "content": "Analyze this CSV and create a summary"}
    ]
)
```

**File handling specifics:**
- Upload via **Files API** (persistent, 500MB/file, 100GB/org) — superior to Assistants' temporary storage
- Use `document` content blocks to reference files by `file_id`
- No built-in "file search" — you manage retrieval (load the file + reference it in context)
- For **RAG over many files**: combine Files API + vector search (Pinecone, Weaviate, etc.) to fetch relevant ones

---

## 2. **Agent SDK + Subagents** (Complex Workflows, Teams)
Best for: Multi-step orchestration, team coordination, isolated task workers, complex reasoning.

**This is the enterprise equivalent** — more powerful than Assistants:

```python
from anthropic import Anthropic
from anthropic_sdk.agent import Agent, agenttools

# Define specialized agents
research_agent = Agent(
    name="research",
    system_prompt="You research topics and find sources...",
    tools=[web_search, code_execution, files]
)

analysis_agent = Agent(
    name="analysis",
    system_prompt="You analyze data and produce reports...",
    tools=[code_execution, files]
)

# Orchestrate via parent agent
response = client.query(
    "Analyze the Q3 sales data and create a forecast",
    agent_tools=[
        agenttools.subagent(research_agent),
        agenttools.subagent(analysis_agent)
    ]
)
```

**Key advantages over Assistants:**
- **Isolated context windows** — each subagent has its own 200K+ context (no pollution)
- **Parallel coordination** — agent teams can work simultaneously
- **Custom hooks** — deterministic automation (before/after events, shell commands)
- **Persistent memory** — via memory tool + CLAUDE.md
- **Code review** — managed PR reviews (Teams/Enterprise)

---

## Migration Path: Assistants → Claude

### **Step 1: Start with Messages API** (Fastest)
If your workflows are straightforward (few steps, single responsibility):

```python
# Replace Assistants API calls with:
messages = []
system = "Your assistant instructions here..."

while True:
    response = client.messages.create(
        model="claude-opus-4-6",
        max_tokens=4096,
        system=system,
        tools=[
            {"type": "code_execution_20260120", "name": "code_execution"},
            # Add web_search, files, etc. as needed
        ],
        messages=messages
    )
    
    # Tool use loop (your orchestration)
    messages.append({"role": "assistant", "content": response.content})
    
    if response.stop_reason == "end_turn":
        break
    
    # Process tool calls, append results, loop again
    for block in response.content:
        if block.type == "tool_use":
            result = process_tool(block.name, block.input)
            messages.append({
                "role": "user",
                "content": [{"type": "tool_result", "tool_use_id": block.id, "content": result}]
            })
```

**Benefits:**
- Familiar control flow
- Can copy Assistants' system prompts directly
- File handling is more explicit (you manage uploads/storage)
- No additional infrastructure

### **Step 2: Move to Agent SDK** (If needed)
Only if you need:
- **Multi-agent coordination** (team/subagent patterns)
- **Hooks for automation** (run shell commands, webhooks after each step)
- **Background tasks** (monitoring, scheduled runs)
- **Code review** (managed PR reviews)

---

## File Handling: Key Differences

| Aspect | OpenAI Assistants | Claude Files API |
|--------|------------------|------------------|
| **Storage** | Temporary (tied to assistant) | Persistent (org-level, 500MB/file) |
| **RAG** | Built-in file search | Manual: load file + reference by ID |
| **Search** | Semantic search over files | You implement retrieval (vector DB recommended) |
| **Cost** | Per-assistant storage | Per-file + per-read tokens |
| **Access** | Auto via assistant | Explicit via content block + `file_id` |

**For file search equivalent:**
```python
# 1. Upload file once
file_response = client.beta.files.upload(
    file=open("data.pdf", "rb"),
    betas=["files-api-2025-04-14"]
)
file_id = file_response.id

# 2. Later: reference in messages
response = client.messages.create(
    model="claude-opus-4-6",
    max_tokens=4096,
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": [
                {"type": "text", "text": "Summarize this document"},
                {"type": "document", "source": {"type": "file", "file_id": file_id}}
            ]
        }
    ]
)
```

For **semantic search** over many files, pair with a vector DB:
```python
# Pseudo-code: RAG pipeline
relevant_files = vector_db.search(query, top_k=3)  # Your vector DB
context_blocks = [
    {"type": "document", "source": {"type": "file", "file_id": fid}}
    for fid in relevant_files
]
response = client.messages.create(
    # ... include context_blocks in messages
)
```

---

## Feature Mapping

| Assistants Feature | Claude Equivalent | Notes |
|-------------------|-------------------|-------|
| **Instructions** | System prompt | Drop-in compatible |
| **File search** | Files API + manual retrieval | More transparent, less automatic |
| **Code interpreter** | `code_execution` tool | Same sandbox, tool-based |
| **Knowledge base** | Files API + Projects (Claude.ai) | Persistent via Projects or memory tool |
| **Conversations** | Message loop + memory tool | You manage persistence |
| **Function calling** | Tool use | Same concept, better streaming |
| **Threads** | Session/conversation object | Implement with message lists |

---

## Recommendation

**Start here:**
1. Use **Messages API** with `code_execution` + `files` tools
2. Migrate your system prompts directly
3. Replace Assistants' tool definitions with Claude tools
4. Build your own orchestration loop (gives you more control anyway)

**Upgrade when needed:**
- Complex multi-agent workflows → **Agent SDK + subagents**
- Persistent context across sessions → **Memory tool** or **Projects** (Claude.ai/Desktop)
- Scheduled automation → **Claude Code** with `/loop` or background tasks

The Messages API is simpler than Assistants for most use cases (no hidden state, explicit tool calls), and you get better file persistence with the Files API.

</details>
